    <div class="post-27 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-art-new-england category-autobiographical-sketches tag-art-new-england tag-carla-munsat tag-dmitri-hadzi tag-ernst-kitziinger tag-flora-natapoff tag-harvard tag-james-ackerman tag-le-corbusier tag-michael-mazur tag-neil-levine tag-sydney-freedberg" id="post-27">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1978/04/the-art-new-england-years/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Becoming an Art Critic">
       Becoming an Art Critic
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       April 13th, 1978
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1978/04/the-art-new-england-years/">
       <img alt="The Shahnameh" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1978/04/shahnameh_mma72_568r_100502-e1274895534946-118x150.jpg" width="118"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       In 1979, an 11th century Persian poem with 50,000 rhyming couplets, illuminated by tiny paintings in exquisite colors made from crushed jewels and insects wings, inspired my first story about art. For the next 20 years, I wrote, published, and broadcast hundreds of Stories about Art in Boston and beyond. This is how it all began.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1978/04/the-art-new-england-years/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Becoming an Art Critic">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/art-new-england/" rel="tag"&gt;Art New England&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/carla-munsat/" rel="tag"&gt;Carla Munsat&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/dmitri-hadzi/" rel="tag"&gt;Dmitri Hadzi&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/ernst-kitziinger/" rel="tag"&gt;Ernst Kitzinger&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/flora-natapoff/" rel="tag"&gt;Flora Natapoff&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/harvard/" rel="tag"&gt;Harvard&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/james-ackerman/" rel="tag"&gt;James Ackerman&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/le-corbusier/" rel="tag"&gt;Le Corbusier&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/michael-mazur/" rel="tag"&gt;Michael Mazur&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/neil-levine/" rel="tag"&gt;Neil Levine&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/sydney-freedberg/" rel="tag"&gt;Sydney Freedberg&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/art-new-england/" rel="category tag"&gt;Art New England&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/autobiographical-sketches/" rel="category tag"&gt;Autobiographical sketches&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1978/04/the-art-new-england-years/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-22 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-art-new-england category-drawing category-museums tag-claude-le-lorrain tag-harvard tag-sackler-museum-harvard tag-tchaikovsky" id="post-22">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1980/04/from-fontainebleau-to-the-louvre/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Claude Le Lorrain">
       Claude Le Lorrain
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       April 1st, 1980
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1980/04/from-fontainebleau-to-the-louvre/">
       <img alt="Claude Lorrain, Apollo And The Muses On Mt Helicon, 1628" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/04/Apollo-And-The-Muses-On-Mt-Helicon-16282-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        CLAUDE
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        LE
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        LORRAIN
       </span>
       depicts the moment just before transfiguration  the moment just before women turn into goddesses, or girls turn into swans, or life turns into art. His light is dusk and twilight  the darkling light that washes the physical world in unearthly beauty and fills the heart with an intoxicating sense of possibility.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1980/04/from-fontainebleau-to-the-louvre/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Claude Le Lorrain">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/claude-le-lorrain/" rel="tag"&gt;Claude Le Lorrain&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/harvard/" rel="tag"&gt;Harvard&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/sackler-museum-harvard/" rel="tag"&gt;Sackler Museum&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/tchaikovsky/" rel="tag"&gt;Tchaikovsky&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/art-new-england/" rel="category tag"&gt;Art New England&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/drawing/" rel="category tag"&gt;Drawing&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/museums/" rel="category tag"&gt;Museums&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1980/04/from-fontainebleau-to-the-louvre/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->
    </div>
    <div class="post-28 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-art-new-england category-museums category-painting tag-abstraction tag-alexei-jawlensky tag-art-new-england tag-busch-reisinger-museum tag-gabriele-munter tag-harvard tag-paul-klee tag-vassily-kandinsky" id="post-28">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1980/11/gabriele-munter-from-munich-to-murnau/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Gabriele Munter: From Munich to Murnau">
       Gabriele Munter: From Munich to Murnau
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       November 1st, 1980
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1980/11/gabriele-munter-from-munich-to-murnau/">
       <img alt='Gabriele Munter, "Breakfast with Birds," 1934' class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1980/11/Gabriele-Fruhstuck-der-Vogel-1934-150x150.png" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       A woman sits thinking, resting her head on her hand in a room filled with flowers and fruit. The room seems charged with meaning, filled with her extraordinary presence. For
       <span class="caps">
        GABRIELE
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        MUNTER
       </span>
       , art was not about appearances, but about realities lying behind appearances. Abstraction was a way of seeing into the heart of things.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1980/11/gabriele-munter-from-munich-to-murnau/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Gabriele Munter: From Munich to Murnau">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/abstraction/" rel="tag"&gt;Abstraction&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/alexei-jawlensky/" rel="tag"&gt;Alexei Jawlensky&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/art-new-england/" rel="tag"&gt;Art New England&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/busch-reisinger-museum/" rel="tag"&gt;Busch-Reisinger Museum.&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/gabriele-munter/" rel="tag"&gt;Gabriele Munter&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/harvard/" rel="tag"&gt;Harvard&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/paul-klee/" rel="tag"&gt;Paul Klee&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/vassily-kandinsky/" rel="tag"&gt;Vassily Kandinsky&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/art-new-england/" rel="category tag"&gt;Art New England&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/museums/" rel="category tag"&gt;Museums&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/painting/" rel="category tag"&gt;Painting&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1980/11/gabriele-munter-from-munich-to-murnau/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-29 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-art-new-england category-drawing category-museums category-painting tag-fogg-museum-harvard tag-harvard tag-jean-auguste-dominique-ingres tag-pablo-picasso tag-paul-cezanne" id="post-29">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1980/12/ingres-1780-1980/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Ingres 1780  1980">
       Ingres 1780  1980
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       December 1st, 1980
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1980/12/ingres-1780-1980/">
       <img alt='J.A.D. Ingres, "Odalisque avec Eslave," Fogg Art Museum' class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1980/12/odalisque-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       For a twentieth-century audience brought up on abstraction,
       <span class="caps">
        INGRES
       </span>
       s greatness, his fascination, lies in the abstract qualities of his line, its restless, obsessive movement across the page. Ingres line has power, grace, life; its brilliant, dramatic, neurotic, even perverse. He told his students, Drawing is everything; it is all of Art.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1980/12/ingres-1780-1980/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Ingres 1780  1980">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/fogg-museum-harvard/" rel="tag"&gt;Fogg Art Museum&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/harvard/" rel="tag"&gt;Harvard&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/jean-auguste-dominique-ingres/" rel="tag"&gt;Jean Auguste Dominique Ingres&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/pablo-picasso/" rel="tag"&gt;Pablo Picasso&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/paul-cezanne/" rel="tag"&gt;Paul Czanne&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/art-new-england/" rel="category tag"&gt;Art New England&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/drawing/" rel="category tag"&gt;Drawing&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/museums/" rel="category tag"&gt;Museums&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/painting/" rel="category tag"&gt;Painting&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1980/12/ingres-1780-1980/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->
    </div>
    <div class="post-31 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-art-new-england category-favorites category-galleries category-painting tag-frances-hamilton" id="post-31">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1981/02/frances-hamilton-books-and-painted-stories/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Frances Hamilton: Books and Painted Stories">
       Frances Hamilton: Books and Painted Stories
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       February 1st, 1981
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1981/02/frances-hamilton-books-and-painted-stories/">
       <img alt="1001 Nights" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1981/02/1001-Nights-e1274409910242-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        FRANCES
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        HAMILTON
       </span>
       has refashioned much-loved images, memories, and dreamstransforming them into a fully re-imagined universe. It is this transformation  the serious, difficult task of art  that gives her work its power to enchant.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1981/02/frances-hamilton-books-and-painted-stories/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Frances Hamilton: Books and Painted Stories">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/frances-hamilton/" rel="tag"&gt;Frances Hamilton&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/art-new-england/" rel="category tag"&gt;Art New England&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/favorites/" rel="category tag"&gt;Favorites&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/galleries/" rel="category tag"&gt;Galleries&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/painting/" rel="category tag"&gt;Painting&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1981/02/frances-hamilton-books-and-painted-stories/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->
    </div>
    <div class="post-104 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-art-new-england category-drawing category-galleries tag-adja-yunkers tag-elizabeth-dworkin tag-gregory-amenoff tag-jake-berthot tag-joan-snyder tag-paul-rotterdam tag-philip-guston tag-porforio-di-donna" id="post-104">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1981/02/work-on-paper/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Work on Paper">
       Work on Paper
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       February 1st, 1981
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1981/02/work-on-paper/">
       <img alt="Philip Guston, Artist in his Studio 1969," class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1982/02/Philip-Guston-artist-in-his-studio-1969--150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Each rectangle is like a picture of a picture, moving through a series of transformations. The tremulous drawings are like jottings, hieroglyphics, messages in bottles, unreadable postcards, ideas coming into being, the first appearances of the not-yet-visible, the impalpable images taking form before our eyes.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1981/02/work-on-paper/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Work on Paper">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-92 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-art-new-england category-museums category-painting tag-cezanne tag-matisse tag-t-s-eliot tag-thomas-mann" id="post-92">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1981/04/the-dial-arts-and-letters-in-the-1920s/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Dial: Arts and Letters in the 1920s">
       The Dial: Arts and Letters in the 1920s
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       April 1st, 1981
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1981/04/the-dial-arts-and-letters-in-the-1920s/">
       <img alt="Matisse, Nasturtiums and the Dance, 1912, Metropolitan Museum of Art" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1981/04/Matisse-Nasturtiums--150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        THE
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        DIAL
       </span>
       was a literary magazine that published T.S. Eliots The Waste Land, Thomas Manns Death in Venice and Virginia Woolfs Mrs. Dalloway, as well as reproductions of artworks collected by Schofield Thayer, a Henry Jamesian character who went abroad in search of old knowledge and new art.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1981/04/the-dial-arts-and-letters-in-the-1920s/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Dial: Arts and Letters in the 1920s">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/cezanne/" rel="tag"&gt;Cezanne&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/matisse/" rel="tag"&gt;Matisse&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/t-s-eliot/" rel="tag"&gt;T.S. Eliot&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/thomas-mann/" rel="tag"&gt;Thomas Mann&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/art-new-england/" rel="category tag"&gt;Art New England&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/museums/" rel="category tag"&gt;Museums&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/painting/" rel="category tag"&gt;Painting&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1981/04/the-dial-arts-and-letters-in-the-1920s/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->
    </div>
    <div class="post-49 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-art-new-england category-interviews category-painting tag-flora-natapoff tag-museum-of-modern-art tag-pieter-brueghel tag-radcliffe" id="post-49">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1981/10/flora-natapoff/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Flora Natapoff">
       Flora Natapoff
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       October 1st, 1981
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1981/10/flora-natapoff/">
       <img alt="Flora Natapoff, 1972." class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/04/FN-Portrait-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       The surface of a
       <span class="caps">
        FLORA
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        NATAPOFF
       </span>
       painting is a place where battles have been fought, cities and temples built up and brought down, and on which there has been a wrestling with angels. The means of expression are abstract  marks on paper and scraps of paper that must always hold their own. But the energy to work comes from looking at something that moves her.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1981/10/flora-natapoff/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Flora Natapoff">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/flora-natapoff/" rel="tag"&gt;Flora Natapoff&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/museum-of-modern-art/" rel="tag"&gt;MOMA&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/pieter-brueghel/" rel="tag"&gt;Pieter Brueghel&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/radcliffe/" rel="tag"&gt;Radcliffe&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/art-new-england/" rel="category tag"&gt;Art New England&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/interviews/" rel="category tag"&gt;Interviews&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/painting/" rel="category tag"&gt;Painting&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1981/10/flora-natapoff/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->
    </div>
    <div class="post-119 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-architecture category-art-new-england category-drawing category-interviews tag-carpenter-center-for-the-visual-arts-harvard tag-harvard tag-john-cage tag-le-corbusier tag-roger-brandenberg-horn tag-william-curtis" id="post-119">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1981/12/the-sketchbooks-of-le-corbusier/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Sketchbooks of Le Corbusier">
       The Sketchbooks of Le Corbusier
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       December 1st, 1981
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1981/12/the-sketchbooks-of-le-corbusier/">
       <img alt="Fondation Le Corbusier, Paris" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1981/12/Fondation-Le-Corbusier-Paris-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        LE
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        CORBUSIER
       </span>
       created his own myth through the organic generation of forms. His genius constantly renewed itself, pulling new phenomena into the orbit of his thought and recreating them in the purified, monumental yet human forms of his architecture.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1981/12/the-sketchbooks-of-le-corbusier/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Sketchbooks of Le Corbusier">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1981/12/kush-lost-kingdom-of-the-nile/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Kush: Lost Kingdom of the Nile">
       Kush: Lost Kingdom of the Nile
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       December 1st, 1981
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1981/12/kush-lost-kingdom-of-the-nile/">
       <img alt="Mask of Queen Malakaye, 6th century BC, MFA Boston" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1981/12/Mask-of-Queen-Malakaye-6th-century-BC3-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>

       <span class="caps">
        KUSH
       </span>
       , Lost Kingdom of the Nile. A meditation on Art, Time, and the ancient river.

     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1982/01/sky-art-conference/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Sky Art Conference">
       Sky Art Conference
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       January 1st, 1982
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1982/01/sky-art-conference/">
       <img alt="Steve Poleskie, smoke trails, 1983" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1982/01/stever-poleskie-1983-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Artists and scientists. working in neon, laser, steam, smoke, video, pyrotechnics, film, inflated and flying sculpture, and other celestial navigations, celebrate the sky as a medium of expression, transmission, and space.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1982/01/sky-art-conference/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Sky Art Conference">
       Read the full article 
      </a>

    <div class="post-116 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-art-new-england category-installation category-interviews tag-center-for-advanced-visual-studies-mit tag-gyorgy-kepes tag-joan-brigham tag-merleau-ponty tag-mit tag-otto-piene tag-sky-art" id="post-116">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1982/05/otto-piene/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Otto Piene">
       Otto Piene
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       May 1st, 1982
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1982/05/otto-piene/">
       <img alt="Otto Piene, Olympic Rainbow, Munich, 1972" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1982/05/Otto-Piene-Olympic-Rainbow-1972-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       As a very young man,
       <span class="caps">
        OTTO
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        PIENE
       </span>
       saw the sky reflected in a sea at long last calm: The feeling of being reborn has never left me. Out of this rebirth came a love for the sky, the desire to point at it, to show how beautiful it is, how it makes us live and feel alive.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1982/05/otto-piene/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Otto Piene">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1982/05/the-drawings-of-andrea-palladio/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Drawings of Palladio">
       The Drawings of Palladio
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       May 1st, 1982
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1982/05/the-drawings-of-andrea-palladio/">
       <img alt="Olympic The - The Stage, Vicenza" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1982/05/Olympic-The-The-Stage-Vicenza2-e1276132357263-138x150.jpg" width="138"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="dquo">
        
       </span>
       There is something divine about his talent, something comparable to the power of a great poet who, out of the worlds of truth and falsehood, creates a third whose borrowed existence enchants us.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1982/05/the-drawings-of-andrea-palladio/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Drawings of Palladio">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/andrea-palladio/" rel="tag"&gt;Andrea Palladio&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/fogg-museum-harvard/" rel="tag"&gt;Fogg Art Museum&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/goethe/" rel="tag"&gt;Goethe&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/venice/" rel="tag"&gt;Venice&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/art-xpress/" rel="category tag"&gt;Art Xpress&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/drawing/" rel="category tag"&gt;Drawing&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/museums/" rel="category tag"&gt;Museums&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1982/05/the-drawings-of-andrea-palladio/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-34 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-art-new-england category-galleries category-painting tag-doug-anderson tag-gerry-bergstein tag-new-wave tag-psychedelic-furs tag-the-talking-heads tag-volker-schlondorff" id="post-34">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1982/06/new-wave-painting/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to New Wave Painting">
       New Wave Painting
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       June 1st, 1982
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1982/06/new-wave-painting/">
       <img alt="psychedelic-furs-debut1" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1982/06/psychedelic-furs-debut1-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       False masks of plastic beauty are among its moving targets. Desperate to survive the glissando of the word processor and the deadly lull of ordinary life, it rips to pieces the worlds fabric and its skin and puts it back together, obsessively recreating from scraps and scrawls and marks and images the objects of its desire and its rage.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1982/06/new-wave-painting/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to New Wave Painting">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-97 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-art-new-england category-galleries tag-abstraction tag-anne-neely tag-robert-ferrandini" id="post-97">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1983/04/anne-neely-robert-ferris-robert-ferrandini/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Anne Neely/Robert Ferrandini">
       Anne Neely/Robert Ferrandini
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       April 1st, 1983
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1983/04/anne-neely-robert-ferris-robert-ferrandini/">
       <img alt="Robert Ferrandini" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1983/04/Ferrandini-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Yet there is exhilaration in the terror, the vertiginous fall. These speedy, violent fantasies of destruction and chaos are tenderly, beautifully described. The drawings in graphite and linseed oil  the oil used wonderfully as color  and the swirls of paint in eerie sea greens or fiery reds compose a balanced, painterly surface. The language of abstraction pulls us upward, as the images plunge us into the abyss.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1983/04/anne-neely-robert-ferris-robert-ferrandini/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Anne Neely/Robert Ferrandini">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/abstraction/" rel="tag"&gt;Abstraction&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/anne-neely/" rel="tag"&gt;Anne Neely&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/robert-ferrandini/" rel="tag"&gt;Robert Ferrandini&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/art-new-england/" rel="category tag"&gt;Art New England&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/galleries/" rel="category tag"&gt;Galleries&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1983/04/anne-neely-robert-ferris-robert-ferrandini/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->
    </div>
    <div class="post-115 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-art-new-england category-prints tag-barbara-krakow-gallery tag-baudelaire tag-deborah-cornell tag-edgar-degas tag-eugenia-parry-janis tag-experimental-etching-studio tag-keats tag-metropolitan-museum-of-art tag-michael-mazur tag-mit tag-monotype tag-ny tag-robert-townsend tag-victoria-munroe" id="post-115">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1983/05/michael-mazur/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Michael Mazur">
       Michael Mazur
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       May 1st, 1983
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1983/05/michael-mazur/">
       <img alt="Michael in his studio" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1983/05/mike_in_studio-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       In
       <span class="caps">
        MICHAEL
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        MAZUR
       </span>
       s hands, the Monotype was the perfect form to convey the multiplicity of life in the natural world. The clearest, most lucid flowers are surrounded by a paler aura of other flowers, other summers, other interpretations  a riot of reeds and flowers, organic growth, confusion, and decay. Revenants of images repeat like ghostly, half-remembered things.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1983/05/michael-mazur/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Michael Mazur">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1983/07/henry-hobson-richardson/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Henry Hobson Richardson">
       Henry Hobson Richardson
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       July 1st, 1983
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1983/07/henry-hobson-richardson/">
       <img alt="HH Richardson portrait by Hubert von Herkomer" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1983/07/HH-Richardson-portrait-by-Hubert-von-Herkomer-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        HENRY
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        HOBSON
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        RICHARDSON
       </span>
       used the colors of the earth like paint, and handled stones and trees with a giants strength and a sculptors grace. The poetry of his architecture makes the stones sing.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1983/07/henry-hobson-richardson/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Henry Hobson Richardson">

     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1984/03/more-than-drawing/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to More Than Drawing">
       More Than Drawing
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       March 1st, 1984
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1984/03/more-than-drawing/">
       <img alt="J.A.D. Ingres, Study for Portrait, 1847, Fogg Art Museum" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1984/03/Study-for-Portrait-of-mme.-Moitessier-1780-1867-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Drawings as a picture making, story telling, dream machine. Drawings that dance, stretch, yearn, arch, and glide across the page. The pleasures of looking emerge here not from what is observed but from how it is rendered; not the image but the artifice.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1984/03/more-than-drawing/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to More Than Drawing">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-114 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-art-new-england category-museums category-painting tag-barbizon tag-chardin tag-jean-francois-millet tag-paris tag-vermeer tag-walt-whitman" id="post-114">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1984/06/jean-francois-millet-seeds-of-impressionism/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Jean-Francois Millet: Seeds of Impressionism">
       Jean-Francois Millet: Seeds of Impressionism
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       June 1st, 1984
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1984/06/jean-francois-millet-seeds-of-impressionism/">
       <img alt="Millet, The Sower, 1850, MFA Boston" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1984/06/Millet-The-Sower-1814-18751-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Jean-Francois
       <span class="caps">
        MILLET
       </span>
       saw a timeless beauty and sadness in life, in evenings dark and filled with color. What I know of happiness is the quiet, the silence, that you can savor so deliciously, either in the forests, or in the fields, he wrote.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1984/06/jean-francois-millet-seeds-of-impressionism/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Jean-Francois Millet: Seeds of Impressionism">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/barbizon/" rel="tag"&gt;Barbizon&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/chardin/" rel="tag"&gt;Chardin&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/jean-francois-millet/" rel="tag"&gt;Jean-Francois Millet&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/paris/" rel="tag"&gt;Paris&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/vermeer/" rel="tag"&gt;Vermeer&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/walt-whitman/" rel="tag"&gt;Walt Whitman&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/art-new-england/" rel="category tag"&gt;Art New England&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/museums/" rel="category tag"&gt;Museums&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/painting/" rel="category tag"&gt;Painting&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1984/06/jean-francois-millet-seeds-of-impressionism/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-117 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-art-new-england category-books category-painting tag-barbara-erlich-white tag-jean-renoir tag-meyer-schapiro tag-paris tag-pierre-auguste-renoir tag-louvre" id="post-117">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1984/12/renoir-a-lesson-in-happiness/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Renoir: A Lesson in Happiness">
       Renoir: A Lesson in Happiness
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       December 1st, 1984
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1984/12/renoir-a-lesson-in-happiness/">
       <img alt="Young Girl Reading. 1886. Oil on canvas. Stdelsches Kunstinstitut und Stdtische Galerie, Frankfurt, Germany." class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1984/12/Young-Girl-Reading.-1886.-Oil-on-canvas.-Stdelsches-Kunstinstitut-und-Stdtische-Galerie-Frankfurt-Germany.--150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="dquo">
        
       </span>
       His hands were terribly deformed. Rheumatism had cracked the joints, bending the thumb toward the palm and the other fingers toward the wrist. Visitors who werent used to it couldnt take their eyes off this mutilation. Their reaction, which they didnt dare express, was: Its not possible. With those hands, he cant paint these pictures. Theres a mystery! The mystery was Renoir himself.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1984/12/renoir-a-lesson-in-happiness/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Renoir: A Lesson in Happiness">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/barbara-erlich-white/" rel="tag"&gt;Barbara Erlich White&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/jean-renoir/" rel="tag"&gt;Jean Renoir&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/meyer-schapiro/" rel="tag"&gt;Meyer Schapiro&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/paris/" rel="tag"&gt;Paris&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/pierre-auguste-renoir/" rel="tag"&gt;Pierre-Auguste Renoir&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/louvre/" rel="tag"&gt;The Louvre&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/art-new-england/" rel="category tag"&gt;Art New England&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/books/" rel="category tag"&gt;Books&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/painting/" rel="category tag"&gt;Painting&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1984/12/renoir-a-lesson-in-happiness/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->
    </div>
    <div class="post-37 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-art-new-england category-galleries category-movies category-painting tag-bertolt-brecht tag-caspar-david-friedrich tag-edvard-munch tag-j-m-w-turner tag-robert-ferrandini" id="post-37">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1984/12/robert-ferrandini/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Robert Ferrandini">
       Robert Ferrandini
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       December 1st, 1984
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1984/12/robert-ferrandini/">
       <img alt="The Day the Earth Stood Still, 1951" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1984/12/Day_the_Earth_Stood_Still_19511-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        ROBERT
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        FERRANDINI
       </span>
       s early work featured flying saucers and monsters, imagery drawn from a 1950s childhood spent watching science-fiction movies like When Worlds Collide and The Thing. In his new paintings of imaginary landscapes and seascapes, he has come to some kind of terms with his past and is ready to move on. His spaceship has finally landed in a world of his own making.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1984/12/robert-ferrandini/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Robert Ferrandini">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

Turner&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/robert-ferrandini/" rel="tag"&gt;Robert Ferrandini&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/art-new-england/" rel="category tag"&gt;Art New England&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/galleries/" rel="category tag"&gt;Galleries&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/movies/" rel="category tag"&gt;Movies&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/painting/" rel="category tag"&gt;Painting&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1984/12/robert-ferrandini/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-38 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-art-new-england category-galleries tag-donald-dreifuss tag-faith-wilding tag-frances-hamilton tag-leslie-sills tag-linda-huey tag-nick-lawrence tag-timothy-nichol" id="post-38">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1985/04/symbolism-animal-as-metaphor/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Animal as Metaphor">
       Animal as Metaphor
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       April 1st, 1985
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1985/04/symbolism-animal-as-metaphor/">
       <img alt="Lascaux Cave drawings" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1985/04/a172lascaux1-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Artists look at animals: the romantic fantasy animal, the primitive art animal, the hidden drives animal, the whimsical animal, the elemental animal, and other mythical beasts. As Walt Whitman wrote,
       <br/>
       I think I could turn and live with animals, they are so placid and self containd,
       <br/>
       I stand and look at them long and long.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1985/04/symbolism-animal-as-metaphor/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Animal as Metaphor">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/donald-dreifuss/" rel="tag"&gt;Donald Dreifuss&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/faith-wilding/" rel="tag"&gt;Faith Wilding&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/frances-hamilton/" rel="tag"&gt;Frances Hamilton&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/leslie-sills/" rel="tag"&gt;Leslie Sills&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/linda-huey/" rel="tag"&gt;Linda Huey&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/nick-lawrence/" rel="tag"&gt;Nick Lawrence&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/timothy-nichol/" rel="tag"&gt;Timothy Nichol&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/art-new-england/" rel="category tag"&gt;Art New England&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/galleries/" rel="category tag"&gt;Galleries&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1985/04/symbolism-animal-as-metaphor/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->
    </div>
    <div class="post-1060 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-autobiographical-sketches category-radio tag-mfa-boston tag-pierre-auguste-renoir tag-radio tag-wbur" id="post-1060">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1985/10/1060/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Radio Days">
       Radio Days
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       October 13th, 1985
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1985/10/1060/">
       <img alt="Rebecca and Alexander, 1985" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/10/Rebecca-and-Alexander-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Something magical happened when the microphone was turned on: all my doubts disappeared. I developed the habit of reading everything out loud, so my writing became more natural and tuned into my voice. I had a huge audience. For the first time in my life, people were listening to what I had to say, and I loved it.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1985/10/1060/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Radio Days">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-459 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-museums category-painting category-radio tag-chao-meng-fu tag-ching-hao tag-daoji tag-harvard tag-sackler-museum-harvard tag-tao-chi tag-wen-c-fong" id="post-459">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1986/05/images-of-the-mind/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Images of the Mind">
       Images of the Mind
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       May 19th, 1986
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1986/05/images-of-the-mind/">
       <img alt="Daoji, Autumn landscape, 1671, Musee Guimet" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/Daoji-1671-Guimet-e1274271208406-116x150.jpg" width="116"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Tao Chi was a prince who became a wandering Buddhist monk. His Melancholy Thoughts on the Hsiao and Hsiang Rivers, captures the mood of the end of autumn. A lonely fishing hut is half-hidden by a few sparse trees; a flock of wild geese flies over a river. The calligraphy echoes the flight of the birds and the quiver of the leaves. Without understanding a word, we can feel the poetry.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1986/05/images-of-the-mind/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Images of the Mind">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/chao-meng-fu/" rel="tag"&gt;Chao Meng-fu&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/ching-hao/" rel="tag"&gt;Ching Hao&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/daoji/" rel="tag"&gt;Daoji&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/harvard/" rel="tag"&gt;Harvard&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/sackler-museum-harvard/" rel="tag"&gt;Sackler Museum&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/tao-chi/" rel="tag"&gt;Tao-chi&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/wen-c-fong/" rel="tag"&gt;Wen C. Fong&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/museums/" rel="category tag"&gt;Museums&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/painting/" rel="category tag"&gt;Painting&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/radio/" rel="category tag"&gt;Radio&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1986/05/images-of-the-mind/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1987/11/john-udvardy/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to John Udvardy">
       John Udvardy
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       November 2nd, 1987
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1987/11/john-udvardy/">
       <img alt="udvardy bittersweeet memories 1987" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1987/11/udvardy-bittersweeet-memories-1987-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Sculptor
       <span class="caps">
        JOHN
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        UDVARDY
       </span>
       sees the aesthetic possibilities in an old whittled paddle or a forked birch branch, and he knows how to make a curve from a green sapling. But most of all, he brings to his materials a feeling that every mark matters: every stick, every thread, every shell, every bone.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1987/11/john-udvardy/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to John Udvardy">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-511 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-galleries tag-frances-hamilton tag-ica tag-tolstoy tag-trustman-gallery tag-war-and-peace" id="post-511">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1988/05/frances-hamilton-pieces-of-time/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Frances Hamilton: Pieces of Time">
       Frances Hamilton: Pieces of Time
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       May 22nd, 1988
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1988/05/frances-hamilton-pieces-of-time/">
       <img alt="France Hamilton, Beastwood Trilogy, 1980" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/Beastwood-e1274492058505-97x150.jpg" width="97"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        FRANCES
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        HAMILTON
       </span>
       s art doesnt come from the head; it comes from the hand and the heart. And thats why a show of her work is always so rewarding. Her images stay with you, growing richer and deeper, as time goes by. They trigger memories. Major or minor, they touch a chord.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1988/05/frances-hamilton-pieces-of-time/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Frances Hamilton: Pieces of Time">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1988/06/contemporary-new-england-furniture/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Contemporary New England Furniture">
       Contemporary New England Furniture
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       June 1st, 1988
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1988/06/contemporary-new-england-furniture/">
       <img alt="Judy McKie, Monkey Chair 1994" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1988/06/monkeychair-1994-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       New England is now the center of an extraordinary flourishing of traditional crafts, especially furniture, because some very talented artists have turned to crafts as a way out of the cynical and cerebral endgame that so much contemporary art is playing today.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1988/06/contemporary-new-england-furniture/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Contemporary New England Furniture">
       Read the full article 
      </a>

     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1988/12/ritsuko-taho/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Ritsuko Taho">
       Ritsuko Taho
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       December 14th, 1988
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1988/12/ritsuko-taho/">
       <img alt="Ritsuko Taho, Duet, Permanent Sculpture Installation, Tokushima, Japan 1996" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1988/12/duet1-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        RITSUKO
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        TAHO
       </span>
       s ever-changing installation is a spare but elegant invitation to participate in a work of art, both literally and metaphorically  by bringing more leaves, and by making a leap of imagination that transforms a heap of trash on a vacant lot into a poem in silver and brown.
      </p>

       Read the full article 
      </a>

    <div class="post-635 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-installation category-movies tag-anna-karina tag-asger-jorn tag-blade-runner tag-christophe-egret tag-cindy-sherman tag-elizabeth-sussman tag-greil-marcus tag-guiseppe-pinot-gallitzia tag-guy-debord tag-ica tag-jay-cantor tag-jean-luc-godard tag-jenny-holzer tag-mark-francis tag-nigel-coates tag-paris tag-peter-wollen tag-situationists tag-thomas-y-levin" id="post-635">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/01/the-situationists/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Situationists">
       The Situationists
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       January 28th, 1989
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/01/the-situationists/">
       <img alt="Guy Debord, Society of the Spectacle" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/situationists2-e1274897141931-114x150.jpg" width="114"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       The Situationists called for an art of excess, delirium, outrage, and social change. They believed that capitalism had turned contemporary life into a society of spectacle that its inhabitants could only passively watch and consume. Situationism would bring art out of the museums and into the streets, and sabotage the society of spectacle by creating situations in which people could turn their own lives into a creative experience.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/01/the-situationists/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Situationists">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/anna-karina/" rel="tag"&gt;Anna Karina&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/asger-jorn/" rel="tag"&gt;Asger Jorn&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/blade-runner/" rel="tag"&gt;Blade Runner&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/christophe-egret/" rel="tag"&gt;Christophe Egret&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/cindy-sherman/" rel="tag"&gt;Cindy Sherman&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/elizabeth-sussman/" rel="tag"&gt;Elizabeth Sussman&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/greil-marcus/" rel="tag"&gt;Greil Marcus&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/guiseppe-pinot-gallitzia/" rel="tag"&gt;Guiseppe Pinot-Gallitzia&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/guy-debord/" rel="tag"&gt;Guy Debord&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/ica/" rel="tag"&gt;ICA&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/jay-cantor/" rel="tag"&gt;Jay Cantor&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/jean-luc-godard/" rel="tag"&gt;Jean-Luc Godard&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/jenny-holzer/" rel="tag"&gt;Jenny Holzer&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/mark-francis/" rel="tag"&gt;Mark Francis&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/nigel-coates/" rel="tag"&gt;Nigel Coates&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/paris/" rel="tag"&gt;Paris&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/peter-wollen/" rel="tag"&gt;Peter Wollen&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/situationists/" rel="tag"&gt;Situationists&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/thomas-y-levin/" rel="tag"&gt;Thomas Y. Levin&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-phoenix/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/installation/" rel="category tag"&gt;Installation&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/movies/" rel="category tag"&gt;Movies&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/01/the-situationists/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->
    </div>
    <div class="post-100 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-art-new-england category-galleries tag-jesseca-ferguson" id="post-100">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/02/jesseca-ferguson-distant-views-and-forgotten-dreams/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Jesseca Ferguson: Distant Views and Forgotten Dreams">
       Jesseca Ferguson: Distant Views and Forgotten Dreams
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       February 1st, 1989
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/02/jesseca-ferguson-distant-views-and-forgotten-dreams/">
       <img alt="Jesseca Ferguson" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1989/02/jesseca-ferguson1-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        JESSECA
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        FERGUSON
       </span>
       s constructions often contain old postcards, which seem to have been sent from places that have long since disappeared. Lost, ruined, or forgotten, they have left behind only pale and ghostly traces. Enshrined in little boxes, like the bones of saints in medieval reliquaries, her work celebrates the sometimes miraculous power of memory to transform the pain and complexity of real life into the stuff of dreams, and art.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/02/jesseca-ferguson-distant-views-and-forgotten-dreams/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Jesseca Ferguson: Distant Views and Forgotten Dreams">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/jesseca-ferguson/" rel="tag"&gt;Jesseca Ferguson&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/art-new-england/" rel="category tag"&gt;Art New England&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/galleries/" rel="category tag"&gt;Galleries&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/02/jesseca-ferguson-distant-views-and-forgotten-dreams/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->
    </div>
    <div class="post-101 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-art-new-england category-museums category-painting tag-anselm-kiefer tag-art-new-england tag-faust tag-goethe tag-jackson-pollock tag-james-joyce tag-joseph-beuys tag-richard-wagner" id="post-101">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/02/anselm-kiefer/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Anselm Kiefer">
       Anselm Kiefer
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       February 1st, 1989
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/02/anselm-kiefer/">
       <img alt="Anselm Kiefer, Brunnhilde Sleeps, 1983, Metropolitan Museum of Art" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1989/02/Anselm-Kiefer-Brunnhilde-Sleeps-1980-Met-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Anselm Kiefer uses the language of modern art to rewrite the kind of grandiose nineteenth-century history painting that modern art rejected. He paints a raging elegy for the failure of reason and civilization to overcome the evil that is part of human nature. Yet for Kiefer, only the magic of art can build something beautiful out of the wreck of reason and the failure of history.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/02/anselm-kiefer/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Anselm Kiefer">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/anselm-kiefer/" rel="tag"&gt;Anselm Kiefer&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/art-new-england/" rel="tag"&gt;Art New England&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/faust/" rel="tag"&gt;Faust&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/goethe/" rel="tag"&gt;Goethe&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/jackson-pollock/" rel="tag"&gt;Jackson Pollock&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/james-joyce/" rel="tag"&gt;James Joyce&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/joseph-beuys/" rel="tag"&gt;Joseph Beuys&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/richard-wagner/" rel="tag"&gt;Richard Wagner&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/art-new-england/" rel="category tag"&gt;Art New England&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/museums/" rel="category tag"&gt;Museums&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/painting/" rel="category tag"&gt;Painting&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/02/anselm-kiefer/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->
    </div>

     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/03/simon-schamas-citizens/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Simon Schamas CITIZENS">
       Simon Schamas
       <span class="caps">
        CITIZENS
       </span>
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       March 7th, 1989
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/03/simon-schamas-citizens/">
       <img alt="J.L.David, Madame Recamier, 1800, Louvre" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1989/12/Madame-Recamaier-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        CITIZENS
       </span>
       , Simon Schamas wonderful new book about the French Revolution, is especially fascinating to people who care about Art, because it is in many ways a book about the power of images to transform the world.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/03/simon-schamas-citizens/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Simon Schamas CITIZENS">
       Read the full article

    <div class="post-512 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-museums category-painting tag-emperor-akihito tag-fujiwara-no-takamitsu tag-genji tag-kino-tomonori tag-kurosawa tag-lady-murasaki-shikibu tag-ono-no-michikaze" id="post-512">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/03/courtly-splendor-twelve-centuries-of-treasures-from-japan/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Courtly Splendor: Twelve Centuries of Treasures from Japan">
       Courtly Splendor: Twelve Centuries of Treasures from Japan
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       March 21st, 1989
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/03/courtly-splendor-twelve-centuries-of-treasures-from-japan/">
       <img alt="Calligraphy by Ono no Michikaze, Tokyo National Museum" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1989/03/Ono-no-Michikaze-Tokyo-National-Museum-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       The silvery glow of the moon and the flow of an underground river are reflected in sinuous calligraphy that swoons down a page from 12th century book of poems, strewn with shimmering silver roses: True, I say nothing/ but the longing in my heart/ reaches out to you,/ secret as the constant flow of an underground river.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/03/courtly-splendor-twelve-centuries-of-treasures-from-japan/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Courtly Splendor: Twelve Centuries of Treasures from Japan">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-477 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-galleries category-painting tag-brancusi tag-decordova-museum-and-sculpture-park tag-roger-kizik" id="post-477">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/04/roger-kizik/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Roger Kizik">
       Roger Kizik
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       April 19th, 1989
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/04/roger-kizik/">
       <img alt="Roger Kizik, The Boathouse, East Anglia, 1998, New Bedford Art Museum" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1989/04/Roger-Kiziks-The-Boathouse-East-Anglia-1998-at-the-New-Bedford-Art-Museum.-Courtesy-of-New-Bedford-Art-Museum1-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        ROGER
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        KIZIK
       </span>
       s loopy, staccato line describes fishing boats with names like Frolic or Finast Kind, houses on the beach, the book he is reading or the tool he is using for fixing up his house or boat. The things in his drawings press in on him; they cluster around him, rich with hidden correspondences and secret messages, composing his life.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/04/roger-kizik/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Roger Kizik">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    </div>
    <div class="post-391 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-galleries category-painting tag-cezanne tag-hiawatha tag-james-fenimore-cooper tag-marty-cain tag-prilla-brackett tag-radcliffe tag-robert-ferrandini tag-watteau" id="post-391">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/05/earth-angels/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Earth Day">
       Earth Day
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       May 7th, 1989
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/05/earth-angels/">
       <img alt="Robert Ferrandini, In Between a Corrosive State and a Disappearing Soul, 1989" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1990/04/Ferrandini-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="dquo">
        
       </span>
       Its all coming from memory, says
       <span class="caps">
        ROBERT
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        FERRANDINI
       </span>
       . From fairy tales, from childhood  from imagining. The way I see it, its the landscape of the mind. Lots of landscapes came to me from the movies. Fort Apache. Red River. Cheyenne Autumn. The Searchers. The idea of the search  which is what I do as a painter. I go into it. I search.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/05/earth-angels/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Earth Day">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-739 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-photography tag-eadweard-muybridge tag-edgar-allan-poe tag-f-holland-day tag-matthew-brady tag-napoleon-sarony tag-susan-sontag" id="post-739">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/06/american-photography-1839-1900/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to American Photography: 1839  1900">
       American Photography: 1839  1900
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       June 2nd, 1989
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/06/american-photography-1839-1900/">
       <img alt="Marcus Aurelius Root, Edgar Allan Poe, 1848" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/06/Marcus-Aurelius-Root-Edgar-Allan-Poe-1848-e1275484347599-143x150.jpg" width="143"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       The people in the portraits present anxious faces to the camera; having your picture taken was a serious business. The camera was enormous, bulky, and expensive; the process was time-consuming and mysterious. Silvery and almost transparent, their delicate faces float on the shimmering silver plates like ghosts.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/06/american-photography-1839-1900/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to American Photography: 1839  1900">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-935 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-drawing category-museums tag-adolph-von-menzel tag-busch-reisinger-museum tag-frederick-the-great tag-peter-nisbet tag-theodor-fontane tag-wagner" id="post-935">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/07/adolph-von-menzel/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Adolph von Menzel">
       Adolph von Menzel
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       July 11th, 1989
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/07/adolph-von-menzel/">
       <img alt="Adolph Menzel - Clara Schumann and  Joseph Joachim" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/06/Adolph-Menzel-Clara-Schumann-und-Joseph-Joachim-SM-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        MENZEL
       </span>
       s drawings often show people and things as if they were turning into shadow, turning into smoke, dissolving into a cloud; just about to disappear. He said, I early cultivated the habit of drawing things as though I were never to see them again.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/07/adolph-von-menzel/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Adolph von Menzel">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/adolph-von-menzel/" rel="tag"&gt;Adolph von Menzel&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/busch-reisinger-museum/" rel="tag"&gt;Busch-Reisinger Museum.&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/frederick-the-great/" rel="tag"&gt;Frederick the Great&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/peter-nisbet/" rel="tag"&gt;Peter Nisbet&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/theodor-fontane/" rel="tag"&gt;Theodor Fontane&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/wagner/" rel="tag"&gt;Wagner&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-phoenix/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/drawing/" rel="category tag"&gt;Drawing&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/museums/" rel="category tag"&gt;Museums&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/07/adolph-von-menzel/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-26 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-museums category-painting category-prints tag-barbara-stern-shapio tag-edgar-degas tag-galeries-durand-ruel tag-henry-james tag-marcel-proust tag-mary-cassatt tag-mfa-boston tag-nancy-mowll-matthews tag-paris tag-virginia-woolf" id="post-26">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/07/mary-cassatt/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Mary Cassatt">
       Mary Cassatt
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       July 14th, 1989
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/07/mary-cassatt/">
       <img alt="mary cassatt letter" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1989/09/mary-cassatt-letter1-e1275958104823-144x150.jpg" width="144"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       In many of the prints, a womans face is partially obscured, either because of the way she has turned her head, or because she is holding something in front of her face  a hand, a letter, a child. This conveys a sense of mystery, a feeling that there are secret meanings and moments of tragedy and what Virginia Woolf called ecstasy  hidden in the texture of a womans daily life.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/07/mary-cassatt/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Mary Cassatt">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-618 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-ceramics category-museums tag-mfa-boston tag-percival-david tag-wu-tung" id="post-618">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/07/imperial-taste/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Imperial Taste">
       Imperial Taste
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       July 24th, 1989
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/07/imperial-taste/">
       <img alt="Imperial Taste" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/imperial_taste-e1274668346959-124x150.jpg" width="124"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       In the 12th century, the Emperor Quianlong, who was a also a poet, said, I want color. He got color: exquisite pale blues and greens that seem to float on the surface of the bowls smooth surfaces like clouds; purple splashes called the sky at dusk; and a pale cobalt blue that seems distilled from a serene and cloudless summer sky.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/07/imperial-taste/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Imperial Taste">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/mfa-boston/" rel="tag"&gt;MFA Boston&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/percival-david/" rel="tag"&gt;Percival David&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/wu-tung/" rel="tag"&gt;Wu Tung&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/ceramics/" rel="category tag"&gt;Ceramics&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/museums/" rel="category tag"&gt;Museums&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/07/imperial-taste/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->
    </div>
    <div class="post-855 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-books category-favorites category-galleries tag-andy-warhol tag-beethoven tag-ed-ruscha tag-karen-meyerhoff-sweet tag-lasse-antonsen tag-marcel-proust tag-milan-kundera tag-sean-licka tag-t-s-eliot tag-the-wizard-of-oz" id="post-855">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/09/ed-ruscha/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Ed Ruscha">
       Ed Ruscha
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       September 8th, 1989
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/09/ed-ruscha/">
       <img alt="Ed Ruscha, Hollywood, 1968" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="108" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/06/Ed-Ruscha-Hollywood-1968-150x108.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       From the window of the studio
       <span class="caps">
        ED
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        RUSCHA
       </span>
       had in the 1960s, he could see a sign reading
       <span class="caps">
        HOLLYWOOD
       </span>
       . The big white letters are as flat an fake as an old, abandoned movie set, crumpled and peeling, with some of the letters falling down. But Ruschas many images of that sign make it a real sign, luminous and charged with light.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/09/ed-ruscha/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Ed Ruscha">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
