     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/09/american-screenprints/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to American Screenprints">
       American Screenprints
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       September 26th, 1989
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/09/american-screenprints/">
       <img alt="Andy Warhol, from 10 Marilyns" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1989/09/Andy-Warhol-from-10-Marilyns-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Many of the most memorable images of the sixties were silkscreen prints: Andy Warhols soupcans, Marilyns, and Jackies, Roy Lichtensteinss day-glo brushstrokes on Ben-Day dots, Sister Coritas Flower Power messages, Robert Indianas
       <span class="caps">
        LOVE
       </span>
       , and Ed Ruschas dazzling 1966 Standard Station, radiant and gleaming in the California light.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/09/american-screenprints/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to American Screenprints">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/12/my-day-without-art/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to My Day Without Art">
       My Day Without Art
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       December 4th, 1989
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/12/my-day-without-art/">
       <img alt="Day Without Art, photo Joe Wrinn" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1989/12/SCAN0023-e1275933989526-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Standing at the center of the spiral, I see the backs of all the chairs facing away from me, and feel a tremendous shock of loneliness and loss. Looking down from the balcony, I see that the chairs are the beginning of a spiral that could go on forever.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/12/my-day-without-art/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to My Day Without Art">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-694 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-museums tag-ellen-rothenberg tag-jesseca-ferguson tag-lois-foster tag-meryl-brater tag-olivia-bernard-wilson tag-robin-shores tag-rose-art-museum tag-william-gibson" id="post-694">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/12/ruins-at-the-rose/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Ruins at the Rose">
       Ruins at the Rose
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       December 8th, 1989
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/12/ruins-at-the-rose/">
       <img alt="Meryl Brater, Form of Language, Rose SArt Museum 1994" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/meryl-formoflanguage-1994-Rose-ASrt-Museum-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       The 80s began with big, shiny, self-confident paintings, but they are ending with of shreds and tatters, and anxious premonitions of a ruined world. They reminded me of the ending of William Gibsons science fiction novel Count Zero, when a brilliant computer distills the few remaining fragments of a ruined civilization into exquisite little constructions. Or these lines from a Shakespeare sonnet; bare, ruined choirs, where late the sweet bird sang.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/12/ruins-at-the-rose/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Ruins at the Rose">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-421 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-photography tag-clifford-ackley tag-meister-eckhart tag-minor-white" id="post-421">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/12/minor-white/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Minor White">
       Minor White
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       December 18th, 1989
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/12/minor-white/">
       <img alt="Barn and Clouds, in the Vicinity of Naples and Dansville, New York 1955" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/12/Barn-and-Clouds-in-the-Vicinity-of-Naples-and-Dansville-New-York-1955--150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        MINOR
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        WHITE
       </span>
       s photographs convey a sense that behind the visible world is another world  a world filled with meaning and magic. He was fascinated by photographys ability to show what he called things for what else they are. He liked to quote the thirteenth-century German mystic Meister Eckhart: The eye with which I see God is the same eye with which God sees me.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/12/minor-white/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Minor White">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/clifford-ackley/" rel="tag"&gt;Clifford Ackley&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/meister-eckhart/" rel="tag"&gt;Meister Eckhart&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/minor-white/" rel="tag"&gt;Minor White&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-phoenix/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/photography/" rel="category tag"&gt;Photography&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1989/12/minor-white/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->
    </div>
    <div class="post-894 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-installation tag-alan-kaprow tag-ica tag-john-cage tag-joseph-beuys tag-robert-rauschenberg tag-william-faulkner tag-yoko-ono" id="post-894">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/01/yoko-ono/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Yoko Ono">
       Yoko Ono
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       January 7th, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/01/yoko-ono/">
       <img alt="Yoko Ono" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/06/Yoko-Ono-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Every viewer who chooses to participate will have a different experience. For me, it was a moving meditation on loss, change, and getting a second chance. As one of the characters in William Faulkners novel The Wild Palms says, Between grief and nothing, I will take grief.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/01/yoko-ono/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Yoko Ono">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/01/robert-whitman/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Robert Whitman">
       Robert Whitman
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       January 14th, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/01/robert-whitman/">
       <img alt="Laurie Anderson, Strange Angels" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1990/01/Laurie-Anderson-Strange-Angels-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       The canvas curled back like a white wave. The light turned red. Silhouettes of dancers moved through the white space like brushstrokes moving across a picture plane. The light turned white. The ceiling rippled and billowed. Silence. White light. I was taking notes, and the only sound I could hear was the sound of my own writing. It was over.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/01/robert-whitman/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Robert Whitman">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-551 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-museums category-photography tag-bertha-wardell tag-carl-zahn tag-charis-weston tag-eadward-weston tag-mfa-boston tag-nat-king-cole tag-theodore-stebbins tag-tina-modotti" id="post-551">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/01/edward-weston-portraits-and-nudes/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Westons Weston: Portraits and Nudes">
       Westons Weston: Portraits and Nudes
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       January 21st, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/01/edward-weston-portraits-and-nudes/">
       <img alt="Tina Modotti, Edward Weston, 1923" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1990/01/Edward_Weston_Tina_Modotti_1923-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        WESTON
       </span>
       s portraits of friends and lovers are so intense that their souls seem to flicker through their sensitive faces and expressive hands. But Westons Nudes are seen in nameless fragments, as cool and smooth as marble. You see their bodies, but their faces are turned away.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/01/edward-weston-portraits-and-nudes/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Westons Weston: Portraits and Nudes">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/bertha-wardell/" rel="tag"&gt;Bertha Wardell&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/carl-zahn/" rel="tag"&gt;Carl Zahn&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/charis-weston/" rel="tag"&gt;Charis Weston&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/eadward-weston/" rel="tag"&gt;Eadward Weston&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/mfa-boston/" rel="tag"&gt;MFA Boston&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/nat-king-cole/" rel="tag"&gt;Nat King Cole&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/theodore-stebbins/" rel="tag"&gt;Theodore Stebbins&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/tina-modotti/" rel="tag"&gt;Tina Modotti&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-phoenix/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/museums/" rel="category tag"&gt;Museums&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/photography/" rel="category tag"&gt;Photography&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/01/edward-weston-portraits-and-nudes/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-633 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-installation tag-cindy-sherman tag-ica tag-plato tag-sophie-calle tag-susan-sontag tag-wittgenstein" id="post-633">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/01/sophie-calle/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Sophie Calle">
       Sophie Calle
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       January 24th, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/01/sophie-calle/">
       <img alt="Sophie Calle" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1990/01/sophie-calle-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        SOPHIE
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        CALLE
       </span>
       borrows elements from detective novels, philosophical investigations, the film noir, the nouveau roman, documentary photography, love letters, art movies, B-movies, John Cages theories of randomness, and Joseph Beuyss actions. She combines them in startling ways, as meditations on the mysterious spaces between self and other.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/01/sophie-calle/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Sophie Calle">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/cindy-sherman/" rel="tag"&gt;Cindy Sherman&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/ica/" rel="tag"&gt;ICA&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/plato/" rel="tag"&gt;Plato&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/sophie-calle/" rel="tag"&gt;Sophie Calle&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/susan-sontag/" rel="tag"&gt;Susan Sontag&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/wittgenstein/" rel="tag"&gt;Wittgenstein&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-phoenix/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/installation/" rel="category tag"&gt;Installation&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/01/sophie-calle/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-469 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-museums category-painting tag-claribel-cone tag-edgar-degas tag-etta-cone tag-gertrude-stein tag-matisse tag-pablo-picasso tag-paul-gauguin tag-pierre-auguste-renoir" id="post-469">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/01/the-cone-collection/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Cone Collection">
       The Cone Collection
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       January 28th, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/01/the-cone-collection/">
       <img alt="Henri Matisse. Purple Robe and Anemones. 1937. The Baltimore Museum of Art" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/Matisse-anemones1-e1274287869226-141x150.jpg" width="141"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       The
       <span class="caps">
        CONE
       </span>
       sisters collected art because they loved it and wanted to live with it. Their art collection became an emblem of their secret selves  a vision of the richness of their inner lives. Many of the images here show women the same expression on their face  a look of contentment, completeness, and self-fulfillment.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/01/the-cone-collection/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Cone Collection">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-571 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-boston-phoenix category-drawing category-museums tag-elizabeth-vigee-lebrun tag-fragonard tag-francesco-guardi tag-francois-boucher tag-giovanni-battista-piranesi tag-mfa-boston tag-talleyrand tag-tiepolo" id="post-571">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/01/the-grand-tour/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Grand Tour">
       The Grand Tour
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       January 28th, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/01/the-grand-tour/">
       <img alt="" class="alignleft wp-post-image tfe" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/FRAGONARD-The-Confession-of-Love-150x150.jpg" title="Fragonard, The Confession of Love, 1777, Frick Collection" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Light as a whisper, these elegant images, in the delicate style known as
       <span class="caps">
        ROCOCO
       </span>
       , convey the sweetness of life before the Revolution. Something of the warmth of the artists hand still lingers in all the little jabs and touches of chalk or ink that make up these delicious little 18th century drawings and prints.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/01/the-grand-tour/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Grand Tour">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-583 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-museums category-textiles tag-francois-boucher tag-john-singer-sargent tag-mfa-boston tag-peter-paul-rubens tag-philippe-de-lasalle tag-rogier-van-der-weyden" id="post-583">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/02/textile-masterpieces/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Textile Masterpieces">
       Textile Masterpieces
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       February 8th, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/02/textile-masterpieces/">
       <img alt="John Singer Sargent, The Daughters of Edward Boit, 1882, MFA Boston" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/thedaughters466-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Rugs and blankets, shrouds and shawls: textiles touched the lives of the people who lived with them. Slumbering in storerooms, rolled up and protected from light, these textile masterpieces have kept their vibrant colors and something of their human warmth. Now, unfurled, they look like magic carpets, poised to rise.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/02/textile-masterpieces/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Textile Masterpieces">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/francois-boucher/" rel="tag"&gt;Francois Boucher&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/john-singer-sargent/" rel="tag"&gt;John Singer Sargent&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/mfa-boston/" rel="tag"&gt;MFA Boston&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/peter-paul-rubens/" rel="tag"&gt;Peter Paul Rubens&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/philippe-de-lasalle/" rel="tag"&gt;Philippe de LaSalle&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/rogier-van-der-weyden/" rel="tag"&gt;Rogier van der Weyden&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-phoenix/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/museums/" rel="category tag"&gt;Museums&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/textiles/" rel="category tag"&gt;Textiles&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/02/textile-masterpieces/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-409 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-archaeological-fragments category-boston-phoenix category-favorites category-galleries category-photography tag-mario-diacono tag-mikedoug-starn tag-titian" id="post-409">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/02/the-starn-twins/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Starn Twins">
       The Starn Twins
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       February 18th, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/02/the-starn-twins/">
       <img alt="Mike and Doug Starn" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/Mike-and-Doug-Starn-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="dquo">
        
       </span>
       It can be frightening, but thats life, said Doug. Art is part of life, said Mike. Its a real part  its the essence of life, said Doug. Theres no reason to make it perfect, says Doug. We want to show the physical nature, said Mike. The physical nature, said Doug. Of everything, but in particular, Art, said Mike.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/02/the-starn-twins/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Starn Twins">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-590 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-galleries category-interviews category-painting tag-antaeus tag-gyorgy-kepes tag-lazlo-moholy-nagy tag-mit" id="post-590">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/03/gyorgy-kepes/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Gyorgy Kepes">
       Gyorgy Kepes
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       March 10th, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/03/gyorgy-kepes/">
       <img alt="Kepes, Untitled, Oil and Sand, 1989" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/Kepes-Untitle-Oil-and-Sand-1989-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        GYORGY
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        KEPES
       </span>
       paints with a mixture of oil paint and sand, which gives his work a rough, earthy texture. He likes to tell the story of Antaeus, a hero who was the son of Mother Earth and could never be defeated as long as he touched the earth. Painting with sand is Kepess way of touching the earth.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/03/gyorgy-kepes/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Gyorgy Kepes">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/03/lou-jones-sojourners-daughters/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Lou Jones: Sojourners Daughters">
       Lou Jones: Sojourners Daughters
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       March 23rd, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/03/lou-jones-sojourners-daughters/">
       <img alt="Lou Jones" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1990/03/LouJones2-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        LOU
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        JONES
       </span>
       s portrait of a musician shows a beautiful old woman with strong hands and a clear, untroubled face. You can feel that shes listening to music; theres a visionary gleam in her eyes. Her portrait is juxtaposed with a faded daguerrotype of a 19th century singer known as the Black Swan.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/03/lou-jones-sojourners-daughters/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Lou Jones: Sojourners Daughters">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-14 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-museums category-painting tag-boston-phoenix tag-isabella-stewart-gardner-museum tag-jan-vermeer tag-keats" id="post-14">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/03/farewell-concert/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Farewell Concert">
       Farewell Concert
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       March 29th, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/03/farewell-concert/">
       <img alt="The Concert by Jan Vermeer" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/03/vermeer-concert-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       I loved
       <span class="caps">
        THE
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        CONCERT
       </span>
       , the beautiful little painting by
       <span class="caps">
        VERMEER
       </span>
       . Each time I looked at it, I saw something new. Now its gone. I try to remember every line, every shadow, every gleam of light, every sweet cadence of its silent music, but I can already feel it fading. As time goes by, it will darken and grow dim.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/03/farewell-concert/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Farewell Concert">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-438 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-galleries category-movies tag-bronzino tag-david-salle tag-douglas-sirk tag-lana-turner tag-mario-diacono tag-museum-of-modern-art" id="post-438">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/03/david-salleimitation-of-life/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to David Salle/Imitation of Life">
       David Salle/Imitation of Life
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       March 29th, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/03/david-salleimitation-of-life/">
       <img alt="Imitation of Life" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1990/03/Imitation-of-Life-e1274221179839-69x150.jpg" width="69"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       One of
       <span class="caps">
        DAVID
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        SALLE
       </span>
       s favorite movies is Douglas Sirks
       <span class="caps">
        IMITATION
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        OF
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        LIFE
       </span>
       . In one scene, all the characters are jammed into a taxi, watching a funeral through the windows. In Salles paintings, too, many different things are happening at once, everything is crammed together, nothing seems finished, everything is seen in reflection or juxtaposition or through a filter or a pane of glass, and all of the contradictions are left unresolved.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/03/david-salleimitation-of-life/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to David Salle/Imitation of Life">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-16 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-dance category-movies tag-ann-miller tag-debbie-reynolds tag-frank-sinatra tag-gene-kelly tag-gershwin tag-leslie-caron tag-shakespeare" id="post-16">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/04/gene-kelly/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Gene Kelly">
       Gene Kelly
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       April 24th, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/04/gene-kelly/">
       <img alt="Singin' in the Rain, 1952, MGM" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/04/singin-in-the-rainthe-good-one-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        GENE
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        KELLY
       </span>
       was a great dancer because his dancing seemed to be an overflow of his superb vitality  a natural extension of his personality. In all his movies, the transitions to dance are incredibly smooth, because even when hes not dancing hes thinking about dancing  his athletic body is flexed and limber and hes ready to roll, even on an empty set with 500,000 kilowatts of electric light mimicking stardust and a giant fan creating the sensation of a moonlight breeze.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/04/gene-kelly/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Gene Kelly">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-628 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-museums category-painting tag-diana-ross tag-mfa-boston tag-monet tag-paul-tucker" id="post-628">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/04/monet-in-the-90s-the-series-paintings/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Monet in the 90s: The Series Paintings">
       Monet in the 90s: The Series Paintings
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       April 30th, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/04/monet-in-the-90s-the-series-paintings/">
       <img alt="Monet in the 90's" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/monet-in-the-90s2-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       In painting after painting, the earth moves and the water swoons and the sky tumbles and all the blues and pinks and purples and reds and oranges dissolve into one. Earth and water come together, again and again, and explode in a symphony of light and color and air.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/04/monet-in-the-90s-the-series-paintings/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Monet in the 90s: The Series Paintings">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/diana-ross/" rel="tag"&gt;Diana Ross&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/mfa-boston/" rel="tag"&gt;MFA Boston&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/monet/" rel="tag"&gt;Monet&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/paul-tucker/" rel="tag"&gt;Paul Tucker&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-phoenix/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/museums/" rel="category tag"&gt;Museums&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/painting/" rel="category tag"&gt;Painting&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/04/monet-in-the-90s-the-series-paintings/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-724 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-museums category-textiles tag-hannah-cohoon tag-mfa-boston" id="post-724">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/05/shaker-spirit-drawings/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Shaker Spirit Drawings">
       Shaker Spirit Drawings
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       May 1st, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/05/shaker-spirit-drawings/">
       <img alt="Hannah Cohoon, Tree of Light" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/Harriet-Cohoon-Tree-of-Light-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       In the nineteenth century, women in Shaker communities recorded their visions of heavenly gardens in spirit or gift drawings  simple gifts that speak to the heart. The words, written in tiny, spidery handwriting, are faded and almost illegible, but the little birds and hearts and flowers make the feelings clear.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/05/shaker-spirit-drawings/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Shaker Spirit Drawings">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/hannah-cohoon/" rel="tag"&gt;Hannah Cohoon&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/mfa-boston/" rel="tag"&gt;MFA Boston&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-phoenix/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/museums/" rel="category tag"&gt;Museums&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/textiles/" rel="category tag"&gt;Textiles&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/05/shaker-spirit-drawings/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->
    </div>
    <div class="post-864 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-autobiographical-sketches category-favorites tag-antonioni tag-bob-dylan tag-cleve-duncan tag-marcel-proust tag-pasadena tag-radcliffe tag-the-beatles" id="post-864">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/05/california-dreamin/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to A California Dream">
       A California Dream
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       May 15th, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/05/california-dreamin/">
       <img alt="Palisades Park jpeg" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1990/05/Palisades-Park-jpeg-e1275963950495-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="dquo">
        
       </span>
       The places we have known do not belong only to the world of space on which we map them for our own convenience. None of them was ever more than a thin slice, held between the contiguous impressions that composed our life at the time; the memory of a particular image is but regret for a particular moment; and houses, roads, avenues are as fugitive, alas, as the years.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/05/california-dreamin/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to A California Dream">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/antonioni/" rel="tag"&gt;Antonioni&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/bob-dylan/" rel="tag"&gt;Bob Dylan&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/cleve-duncan/" rel="tag"&gt;Cleve Duncan&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/marcel-proust/" rel="tag"&gt;Marcel Proust&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/pasadena/" rel="tag"&gt;Pasadena&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/radcliffe/" rel="tag"&gt;Radcliffe&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/the-beatles/" rel="tag"&gt;The Beatles&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/autobiographical-sketches/" rel="category tag"&gt;Autobiographical sketches&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/favorites/" rel="category tag"&gt;Favorites&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/05/california-dreamin/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-729 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-museums category-prints tag-frank-stella tag-mfa-boston tag-robert-rauschenberg tag-titian" id="post-729">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/05/robert-rauschenberg/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Robert Rauschenberg">
       Robert Rauschenberg
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       May 22nd, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/05/robert-rauschenberg/">
       <img alt="Rauschenberg- Scenarios" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1990/05/Rauschenberg-Scenarios1-e1275182638178-120x150.jpg" width="120"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Great art cheats death of its victory by transforming memorys fragile fragments into something lasting, precious, and incorruptible. The ghostly white porch is a window to a world beyond flesh and paint  a world without sorrow or substance, color or weight. It is cool, pale, and white as a bone.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/05/robert-rauschenberg/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Robert Rauschenberg">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/05/jean-arthur/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Jean Arthur">
       Jean Arthur
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       May 30th, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/05/jean-arthur/">
       <img alt="Jean Arthur" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/04/jean-arthur-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       On film,
       <span class="caps">
        JEAN
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        ARTHUR
       </span>
       is impulsive, but truthful  true to the moment, while the moment lasts. She is chaste, but not prudish; she truly inhabits her small, athletic body, and she moves like a dancer with an easy natural voluptuousness. Her soft, gravelly voice is astonishly expressive. And some of her greatest lines arent words at all, but an astonishing repertoire of whimpers, sighs, sobs, giggles, and moans.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/05/jean-arthur/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Jean Arthur">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/cary-grant/" rel="tag"&gt;Cary Grant&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/frank-capra/" rel="tag"&gt;Frank Capra&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/george-stevens/" rel="tag"&gt;George Stevens&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/howard-hawks/" rel="tag"&gt;Howard Hawks&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/jean-arthur/" rel="tag"&gt;Jean Arthur&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/joel-mccrea/" rel="tag"&gt;Joel McCrea&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-phoenix/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/favorites/" rel="category tag"&gt;Favorites&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/movies/" rel="category tag"&gt;Movies&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/05/jean-arthur/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/06/madame-de-pompadour/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Madame de Pompadour">
       Madame de Pompadour
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       June 1st, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/06/madame-de-pompadour/">
       <img alt="Francois Boucher, Madame de Pompadour, National Gallery of Art,Scotland" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/06/Francois-Boucher-Madame-de-Pompadour-1721-1764-National-Gallery-of-Art--150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Madame de Pompadour always managed to look graceful, even in the most constricting clothes  corsets, bustles, and stays. Like Madonna, she created a Look that was supremely artificial  the powdered hair, the heavily applied make-up, the elaborate gowns. Like Madonna in her John-Paul Gaultier bustiers, La Pompadour in her neglige proudly displayed her sexuality as the source of her power.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/06/madame-de-pompadour/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Madame de Pompadour">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/dick-tracy/" rel="tag"&gt;Dick Tracy&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/francois-boucher/" rel="tag"&gt;Francois Boucher&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/john-paul-gaultier/" rel="tag"&gt;John-Paul Gaultier&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/madame-de-pompadour/" rel="tag"&gt;Madame de Pompadour&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/madonna/" rel="tag"&gt;Madonna.&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/versailles/" rel="tag"&gt;Versailles&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-phoenix/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/favorites/" rel="category tag"&gt;Favorites&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/museums/" rel="category tag"&gt;Museums&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/music/" rel="category tag"&gt;Music&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/painting/" rel="category tag"&gt;Painting&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/theater/" rel="category tag"&gt;Theater&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/06/madame-de-pompadour/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-910 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix tag-byron-rushing tag-dante tag-david-freedberg tag-ica tag-jane-kardon tag-john-milton tag-milan-kundera tag-robert-mapplethorpe tag-saint-augustine tag-wagner" id="post-910">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/06/censorship-and-the-arts/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Censorship and the Arts">
       Censorship and the Arts
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       June 9th, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/06/censorship-and-the-arts/">
       <img alt="Goya, The Sleep of Reason Produces Monsters" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1990/06/Goya-The-Sleep-of-Reason-Produces-Monsters-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       It takes a lot of courage to be an artist. All kinds of things get in the way, but the thing that gets in the way the most is fear. Thats why the threat of censorship is so dangerous to Art. Art helps us to see the beautiful  and also to face the ugliness in life. Artists need to be free to show us the world as they see it  to tell it like it is.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/06/censorship-and-the-arts/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Censorship and the Arts">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-929 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-furniture category-interviews tag-judy-kensley-mckie tag-rhode-island-school-of-design tag-rose-art-museum tag-todd-mckie tag-wittgenstein" id="post-929">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/06/judy-kensley-mckie-and-todd-mckie/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Judy Kensley McKie and Todd McKie">
       Judy Kensley McKie and Todd McKie
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       June 15th, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/06/judy-kensley-mckie-and-todd-mckie/">
       <img alt="Judy McKie, American Craft Magazine" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/06/Judy-McKie-American-Craft-Magazine-e1276219860469-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       In 1969,
       <span class="caps">
        TODD
       </span>
       and
       <span class="caps">
        JUDY
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        MCKIE
       </span>
       painted banners with the signs of the Zodiac for Woodstock, which people pulled down to use as tents and blankets in the rain. Judy began making furniture in the early 70s to furnish their apartment. One day she impulsively carved two crouching figures into the arms of a butcherblock couch.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/06/judy-kensley-mckie-and-todd-mckie/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Judy Kensley McKie and Todd McKie">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/judy-kensley-mckie/" rel="tag"&gt;Judy Kensley McKie&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/rhode-island-school-of-design/" rel="tag"&gt;Rhode Island School of Design&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/rose-art-museum/" rel="tag"&gt;Rose Art Museum&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/todd-mckie/" rel="tag"&gt;Todd McKie&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/wittgenstein/" rel="tag"&gt;Wittgenstein&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-phoenix/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/furniture/" rel="category tag"&gt;Furniture&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/interviews/" rel="category tag"&gt;Interviews&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/06/judy-kensley-mckie-and-todd-mckie/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-833 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-dance category-galleries tag-cole-porter tag-fred-astaire tag-ginger-rogers tag-louis-cartier" id="post-833">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/06/louis-cartier/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Louis Cartier">
       Louis Cartier
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       June 22nd, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/06/louis-cartier/">
       <img alt="Ginger Rogers" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/06/Ginger-Rogers-e1275911505794-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        LOUIS
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        CARTIER
       </span>
       used precious metals and jewels in a highly polished, sparkling, and yet almost casual way way  the way Fred Astaire and Ginger Rogers danced. The shimmer of dozens of tiny diamonds on a cool platinum surface is the essence of sophistication - like a Cole Porter song.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/06/louis-cartier/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Louis Cartier">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-821 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-installation category-interviews tag-matt-mullican tag-mit" id="post-821">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/07/matt-mullican/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Matt Mullican">
       Matt Mullican
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       July 6th, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/07/matt-mullican/">
       <img alt="Matt Mullican, A Drawing Translates the Way of Thinking" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/06/Matt-Mullican-A-Drawing-Translates-the-Way-of-Thinking-e1275826320775-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Being inside
       <span class="caps">
        MATT
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        MULLICAN
       </span>
       s installation is like being inside Matt Mullicans mind  a dizzying experience. Hes constantly classifying and re-ordering everything. Its the first time Ive arranged my meaning as objects in space depicting my meaning, he says.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/07/matt-mullican/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Matt Mullican">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/matt-mullican/" rel="tag"&gt;Matt Mullican&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/mit/" rel="tag"&gt;MIT&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-phoenix/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/installation/" rel="category tag"&gt;Installation&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/interviews/" rel="category tag"&gt;Interviews&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/07/matt-mullican/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->
    </div>
    <div class="post-717 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-museums category-sculpture tag-audubon tag-kathy-halbreich tag-longfellow tag-martin-puryear tag-mfa-boston tag-trevor-fairbrother tag-william-butler-yeats" id="post-717">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/07/martin-puryear/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Martin Puryear">
       Martin Puryear
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       July 9th, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/07/martin-puryear/">
       <img alt="Martin Puryear, Catalogue, MOMA" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/Martin-Puryear-Catalogue-MOMA-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       His falcons are elegant objects, yet they are also birds of prey. They are chained to a perch, dreaming of flight; perfectly at rest, yet poised to spread their wings and reach for the sky. His art conveys a sense of scraping away and discarding everything that is not essential  of travelling light, like a nomad, and soaring high, like a bird.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/07/martin-puryear/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Martin Puryear">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-916 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-museums category-uncategorized tag-boucher tag-ibsen tag-mfa-boston tag-paul-verlaine tag-pierre-bonnard tag-proust tag-sappho tag-stephane-mallarme" id="post-916">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/09/pierre-bonnard-prints/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Pierre Bonnard: Prints">
       Pierre Bonnard: Prints
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       September 1st, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/09/pierre-bonnard-prints/">
       <img alt="Bonnard, Verlaine, Parallelement" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="135" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/06/Bonnard-Verlaine-Parallelement-e1276569762270-150x135.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        BONNARD
       </span>
       s art is an art of nuance and suggestion. His friend, the Symbolist poet Paul Verlaine, wrote:
       <br/>
       You must have music first of all,
       <br/>
       and for that a rhythm uneven is best,
       <br/>
       vague in the air and soluble
       <br/>
       with nothing heavy and nothing at rest.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/09/pierre-bonnard-prints/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Pierre Bonnard: Prints">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-1032 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-museums tag-charles-francois-daubigny tag-mfa-boston tag-monet tag-narcisse-virgile-diaz-de-la-pena tag-sackler-museum-harvard tag-theodore-rousseau tag-vincent-van-gogh tag-william-morris-hunt" id="post-1032">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/10/barbizon/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Barbizon">
       Barbizon
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       October 1st, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/10/barbizon/">
       <img alt="Millet, The Gleaners, Musee d'Orsay" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/06/Millet-The-Gleaners-Musee-dOrsay-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Barbizon was a place and a style  and also a feeling  a mood  a time of day  dusk, when the forms of things soften and the edges blur, and a kind of hush falls over the world. The earth is solemn, soft, and tender, like a bed  and sometimes like a grave.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/10/barbizon/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Barbizon">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/charles-francois-daubigny/" rel="tag"&gt;Charles-Franois Daubigny&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/mfa-boston/" rel="tag"&gt;MFA Boston&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/monet/" rel="tag"&gt;Monet&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/narcisse-virgile-diaz-de-la-pena/" rel="tag"&gt;Narcisse-Virgile Diaz de la Pea&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/sackler-museum-harvard/" rel="tag"&gt;Sackler Museum&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/theodore-rousseau/" rel="tag"&gt;Thodore Rousseau&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/vincent-van-gogh/" rel="tag"&gt;Vincent van Gogh&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/william-morris-hunt/" rel="tag"&gt;William Morris Hunt&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-phoenix/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/museums/" rel="category tag"&gt;Museums&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/10/barbizon/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->
    </div>
    <div class="post-843 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-galleries category-sculpture tag-chuck-holtzman" id="post-843">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/11/chuck-holtzman/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Chuck Holtzman">
       Chuck Holtzman
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       November 7th, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/11/chuck-holtzman/">
       <img alt="Chuck Holtzman, Untitled 2010" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1990/11/Chuck-Holtzman-Untitled-2010-e1275936300574-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       His sculpture is like a very sophisticated game of musical chairs, where all the pieces come together for a moment of perfect, precarious balance. In his drawings, the charcoal keeps on dancing, long after the music stops.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/11/chuck-holtzman/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Chuck Holtzman">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/chuck-holtzman/" rel="tag"&gt;Chuck Holtzman&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-phoenix/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/galleries/" rel="category tag"&gt;Galleries&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/sculpture/" rel="category tag"&gt;Sculpture&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/11/chuck-holtzman/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-846 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-photography" id="post-846">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/11/linda-connor/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Linda Connor">
       Linda Connor
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       November 7th, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/11/linda-connor/">
       <img alt="Linda Connor, Hagia Sophia, Istanbul, 2005" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1990/11/Linda-Connor-Hagia-Sophia-Istanbul-2005-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       In
       <span class="caps">
        LINDA
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        CONNOR
       </span>
       s cameras mystical eye, the world is filled with ancient sacred things. The same images repeat and recur in her body of work  spirals, veils, beams of light shining into a dark place, open doors, closed eyes, hands  but each time you see them, they mean something different. Each time you see them, they mean something more.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/11/linda-connor/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Linda Connor">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-882 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-museums category-painting tag-carl-and-edith-weyerhaeuser tag-duxbury tag-kojiro-tomita tag-tomita-kohichi" id="post-882">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/11/a-tribute-to-kojiro-tomita/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to A Tribute to Kojiro Tomita">
       A Tribute to Kojiro Tomita
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       November 8th, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/11/a-tribute-to-kojiro-tomita/">
       <img alt="Chu Ta, 1626-1705" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1990/11/Chu-Ta-1626-1705-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       It is said that
       <span class="caps">
        CHU
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        TA
       </span>
       never spoke  but he laughed, cried, waved his hands, and drank rice wine most expressively while he painted. Every single touch of Chu Tas brush means something. Every mark still matters. Hundreds of years later, you can still almost feel the movement of his hand  the bold drunken touch of his brush.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/11/a-tribute-to-kojiro-tomita/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to A Tribute to Kojiro Tomita">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/carl-and-edith-weyerhaeuser/" rel="tag"&gt;Carl and Edith Weyerhaeuser&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/duxbury/" rel="tag"&gt;Duxbury.&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/kojiro-tomita/" rel="tag"&gt;Kojiro Tomita&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/tomita-kohichi/" rel="tag"&gt;Tomita Kohichi&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-phoenix/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/museums/" rel="category tag"&gt;Museums&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/painting/" rel="category tag"&gt;Painting&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/11/a-tribute-to-kojiro-tomita/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-452 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-museums category-prints tag-clifford-ackley tag-helen-frankenthaler tag-joan-snyder tag-john-cage tag-john-chamberlain tag-mary-frank tag-melissa-johnson tag-mfa-boston tag-michael-mazur tag-ovid tag-pat-steir tag-pegasus tag-persephone tag-stanley-boxer tag-walter-pater" id="post-452">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/12/the-unique-print/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Unique Print">
       The Unique Print
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       December 9th, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/12/the-unique-print/">
       <img alt="Mary Frank, Fern,1986, MFA Boston" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1990/12/Mary-Frank-Fern--150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       In monotype, there is no fixed image on the printing surface. The artist paints or draws on a printing plate, makes changes, and prints again; the final proof is an accumulation of all the changes that have been made. Pale, faded images of past impressions often cling to monotypes like shadows; they are called ghosts.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/12/the-unique-print/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Unique Print">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/clifford-ackley/" rel="tag"&gt;Clifford Ackley&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/helen-frankenthaler/" rel="tag"&gt;Helen Frankenthaler&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/joan-snyder/" rel="tag"&gt;Joan Snyder&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/john-cage/" rel="tag"&gt;John Cage&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/john-chamberlain/" rel="tag"&gt;John Chamberlain&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/mary-frank/" rel="tag"&gt;Mary Frank&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/melissa-johnson/" rel="tag"&gt;Melissa Johnson&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/mfa-boston/" rel="tag"&gt;MFA Boston&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/michael-mazur/" rel="tag"&gt;Michael Mazur&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/ovid/" rel="tag"&gt;Ovid&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/pat-steir/" rel="tag"&gt;Pat Steir&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/pegasus/" rel="tag"&gt;Pegasus&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/persephone/" rel="tag"&gt;Persephone&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/stanley-boxer/" rel="tag"&gt;Stanley Boxer&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/walter-pater/" rel="tag"&gt;Walter Pater&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-phoenix/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/museums/" rel="category tag"&gt;Museums&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/prints/" rel="category tag"&gt;Prints&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/12/the-unique-print/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-342 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-galleries category-installation tag-dana-friis-hansen tag-howard-yezerski-gallery tag-jean-auguste-dominique-ingres tag-lillian-hsu-flanders tag-mags-harries tag-mit tag-nan-goldin" id="post-342">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/12/love-and-death/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Love and Death">
       Love and Death
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       December 14th, 1990
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/12/love-and-death/">
       <img alt="Ingres, Raphael and the Fornarina, 1812, Fogg Art Museum" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/IngresRaffaelAndFornarina-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       The prayers were long, thin strips of paper or canvas, newsprint, photographs, or tinsel, embellished with drawings, paint, cutouts, dried roses, gold leaf, buttons, beads. Some were abstract; some had words; others had musical notations written on them. One prayer was made from a piece of old, paintsplattered blue jeans, with a peace symbol and love beads.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/12/love-and-death/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Love and Death">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/dana-friis-hansen/" rel="tag"&gt;Dana Friis-Hansen&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/howard-yezerski-gallery/" rel="tag"&gt;Howard Yezerski Gallery&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/jean-auguste-dominique-ingres/" rel="tag"&gt;Jean Auguste Dominique Ingres&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/lillian-hsu-flanders/" rel="tag"&gt;Lillian Hsu-Flanders&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/mags-harries/" rel="tag"&gt;Mags Harries&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/mit/" rel="tag"&gt;MIT&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/nan-goldin/" rel="tag"&gt;Nan Goldin&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-phoenix/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/galleries/" rel="category tag"&gt;Galleries&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/installation/" rel="category tag"&gt;Installation&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1990/12/love-and-death/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->
    </div>
    <div class="post-634 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-installation category-interviews tag-alexander-brodsky tag-andrei-filippov tag-david-ross tag-dostoevski tag-elena-elagina tag-elizabeth-sussman tag-ica tag-ilya-kabakov tag-ilya-utkin tag-joseph-bakshtein tag-komar-and-melamid tag-margarita-tupitsyn" id="post-634">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/01/ilya-kabakovsoviet-conceptual-art/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Ilya Kabakov/Soviet Conceptual Art">
       Ilya Kabakov/Soviet Conceptual Art
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       January 6th, 1991
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/01/ilya-kabakovsoviet-conceptual-art/">
       <img alt="Ilya Kabakov , Phaidon" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/Kabakov-Phaidon-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       When you look up, all those fragments convey a vertiginous sense of disintegration, and decay. But when you look down, everything is compressed onto a single shiny surface, and its beautiful. All that debris  all that waste and pain  is transformed into art.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/01/ilya-kabakovsoviet-conceptual-art/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Ilya Kabakov/Soviet Conceptual Art">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/alexander-brodsky/" rel="tag"&gt;Alexander Brodsky&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/andrei-filippov/" rel="tag"&gt;Andrei Filippov'&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/david-ross/" rel="tag"&gt;David Ross&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/dostoevski/" rel="tag"&gt;Dostoevski&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/elena-elagina/" rel="tag"&gt;Elena Elagina&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/elizabeth-sussman/" rel="tag"&gt;Elizabeth Sussman&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/ica/" rel="tag"&gt;ICA&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/ilya-kabakov/" rel="tag"&gt;Ilya Kabakov&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/ilya-utkin/" rel="tag"&gt;Ilya Utkin&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/joseph-bakshtein/" rel="tag"&gt;Joseph Bakshtein&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/komar-and-melamid/" rel="tag"&gt;Komar and Melamid&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/margarita-tupitsyn/" rel="tag"&gt;Margarita Tupitsyn&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/installation/" rel="category tag"&gt;Installation&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/interviews/" rel="category tag"&gt;Interviews&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/01/ilya-kabakovsoviet-conceptual-art/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-404 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-installation category-theater tag-einstein tag-frederick-the-great tag-gluck tag-hans-peter-kuhn tag-maria-callas tag-medea tag-mfa-boston tag-napoleon tag-robert-wilson tag-sans-souci tag-sherryl-sutton tag-trevor-fairbrother tag-versailles tag-willaim-wetmore-story" id="post-404">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/01/robert-wilsons-vision/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Robert Wilsons Vision">
       Robert Wilsons Vision
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       January 17th, 1991
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/01/robert-wilsons-vision/">
       <img alt="Robert Wilson" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/vision-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        ROBERT
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        WILSON
       </span>
       S
       <span class="caps">
        VISION
       </span>
       is structured like a journey  a journey that moves from morning to night  from white to black  from the past to the future  from birth to death. A journey that has no beginning and no end, but all takes place in a timeless, endless present.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/01/robert-wilsons-vision/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Robert Wilsons Vision">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-386 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-interviews category-music category-theater tag-a-r-t tag-berlin tag-hans-peter-kuhn tag-ibsen tag-jutta-lampe tag-maria-callas tag-maxxi-rome tag-mfa-boston tag-robert-wilson tag-sasha-waltz tag-trevor-fairbrother" id="post-386">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/02/the-sound-artist-hans-peter-kuhn/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Sound Artist: Hans Peter Kuhn">
       The Sound Artist: Hans Peter Kuhn
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       February 18th, 1991
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/02/the-sound-artist-hans-peter-kuhn/">
       <img alt="Hans Peter Kuhn at the Mattress Factory" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/HPK-Mattress-Factory-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="dquo">
        
       </span>
       Sound art is more open and much closer to life than music. Music is a filtered experience. Im not a composer. I dont want the emotional view bound or directed in any one direction. I want to keep it open. Im always trying things out. I hear something and I can pick it up and react in minutes. Im interested in everything that makes a noise.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/02/the-sound-artist-hans-peter-kuhn/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Sound Artist: Hans Peter Kuhn">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/a-r-t/" rel="tag"&gt;A.R.T.&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/berlin/" rel="tag"&gt;Berlin&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/hans-peter-kuhn/" rel="tag"&gt;Hans Peter Kuhn&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/ibsen/" rel="tag"&gt;Ibsen&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/jutta-lampe/" rel="tag"&gt;Jutta Lampe&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/maria-callas/" rel="tag"&gt;Maria Callas&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/maxxi-rome/" rel="tag"&gt;MAXXI Rome&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/mfa-boston/" rel="tag"&gt;MFA Boston&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/robert-wilson/" rel="tag"&gt;Robert Wilson&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/sasha-waltz/" rel="tag"&gt;Sasha Waltz&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/trevor-fairbrother/" rel="tag"&gt;Trevor Fairbrother&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-phoenix/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/interviews/" rel="category tag"&gt;Interviews&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/music/" rel="category tag"&gt;Music&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/theater/" rel="category tag"&gt;Theater&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/02/the-sound-artist-hans-peter-kuhn/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-531 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-sculpture category-theater tag-charles-honi-coles tag-ibsen tag-robert-wilson tag-sheryl-sutton" id="post-531">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/02/when-we-dead-awaken/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to When We Dead Awaken">
       When We Dead Awaken
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       February 21st, 1991
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/02/when-we-dead-awaken/">
       <img alt="When We Dead Awaken at the ART" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1991/02/SCAN0021-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       A neon blue river of light crosses the stage on a diagonal. A black mountain looms beyond, pierced by a stark white waterfall. The sculptor sits brooding on a rocky throne; an egg-shaped stone is pierced with a spear. Two Irenes enter, and lie on the ground, like stones. You have killed my soul, they cry. I am an artist! cries the sculptor. One Irene sits on the rock, like a statue. I was a human being too.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/02/when-we-dead-awaken/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to When We Dead Awaken">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/charles-honi-coles/" rel="tag"&gt;Charles "Honi" Coles&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/ibsen/" rel="tag"&gt;Ibsen&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/robert-wilson/" rel="tag"&gt;Robert Wilson&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/sheryl-sutton/" rel="tag"&gt;Sheryl Sutton&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-phoenix/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/sculpture/" rel="category tag"&gt;Sculpture&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/theater/" rel="category tag"&gt;Theater&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/02/when-we-dead-awaken/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->
