     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/03/where-all-ladders-start/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Future of Art">
       The Future of Art
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       March 1st, 1991
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/03/where-all-ladders-start/">
       <img alt="Marion Parry, gouache for cover, Radcliffe Quarterly, 1991, Collection of Rebecca Nemser" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1991/03/radcliffecover-e1274493024363-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       It is art that acknowledges the struggle of its own making, and conveys a sense of life as composed of fragments, where not everything is legible, and some things are irrevocably ruined or lost. The past haunts and enriches the present. Memory and imagination are intertwined. It is a mirror of the soul.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/03/where-all-ladders-start/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Future of Art">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-1023 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-drawing category-museums tag-david-stone tag-guercino tag-sackler-museum-harvard" id="post-1023">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/03/guercino/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Guercino">
       Guercino
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       March 14th, 1991
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/03/guercino/">
       <img alt="Guercino, Master Draftsman" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="138" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/06/SCAN0026-e1276545163271-150x138.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        GUERCINO
       </span>
       drew like an angel  his gorgeous line curls across the page; his brush forms shadows that suggest a sense of the roundness and fullness of life. His best drawings are more than drawings  they are blessings, exquisite expressions of those moments when Art and Faith are one.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/03/guercino/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Guercino">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/david-stone/" rel="tag"&gt;David Stone&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/guercino/" rel="tag"&gt;Guercino&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/sackler-museum-harvard/" rel="tag"&gt;Sackler Museum&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/drawing/" rel="category tag"&gt;Drawing&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/museums/" rel="category tag"&gt;Museums&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/03/guercino/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-18 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-photography tag-boston-athenaeum tag-olivia-parker tag-rosamond-w-purcell tag-siegfried-giediion tag-stephen-jay-gould tag-susan-sontag" id="post-18">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/03/photography-at-the-boston-athenaeum/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Photography at the Boston Athenaeum">
       Photography at the Boston Athenaeum
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       March 28th, 1991
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/03/photography-at-the-boston-athenaeum/">
       <img alt="The Boston Athenaeum" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/04/The-Boston-Athenaeum-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       The Boston Athenaeum, a Library with gracious high-ceilinged rooms adorned with columns and all kinds of Graeco-Roman architectural details, and filled with books and pictures, was built by 19th century Bostonians as a modern temple to Athena, Goddess of Wisdom.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/03/photography-at-the-boston-athenaeum/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Photography at the Boston Athenaeum">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/boston-athenaeum/" rel="tag"&gt;Boston Athenaeum&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/olivia-parker/" rel="tag"&gt;Olivia Parker&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/rosamond-w-purcell/" rel="tag"&gt;Rosamond W.     <div class="post-20 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-drawing tag-boston-center-for-the-arts tag-candace-walter tag-charles-kanwischer tag-cherryl-warrick tag-chuck-holtzman tag-clifford-ackley tag-gabriel-garcia-marquez tag-gerry-bergstein tag-john-wilson tag-meryl-brater tag-mfa-boston tag-michael-mazur tag-tao-chi" id="post-20">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/04/12th-annual-boston-drawing-show/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to 12th Annual Boston Drawing Show">
       12th Annual Boston Drawing Show
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       April 13th, 1991
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/04/12th-annual-boston-drawing-show/">
       <img alt="Gerry Bergstein, Entropy #3, 1992" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1991/04/Bergsein-Entropy-3-1992-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        GERRY
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        BERGSTEIN
       </span>
       s drawings show scribbles, scrawls, crossings-out, angry re-workings, markings of struggle and doubt. From this chaos of marks on paper emerge luminous little still lives, marked by the process of decay: visions of a world in flux, where everything is changing, growing, living, dying, and being reborn.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/04/12th-annual-boston-drawing-show/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to 12th Annual Boston Drawing Show">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-630 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-installation tag-annette-lemieux tag-arnulf-rainer tag-cindy-sherman tag-descartes tag-elizabeth-sussman tag-ica tag-rosemarie-trockel tag-sidra-stich tag-sigmar-polke tag-sophie-calle" id="post-630">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/05/rosemarie-trockel/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Rosemarie Trockel">
       Rosemarie Trockel
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       May 25th, 1991
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/05/rosemarie-trockel/">
       <img alt="Rosemarie Trockel" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1989/05/rosemarie-trockel-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="dquo">
        
       </span>
       All these images are obliterated, defaced, lost. Its about those marginal, mundane experiences that are for some reason significant to her. There are certain things about her work that are mysterious. They remain mysterious. And she treasures that mysteriousness.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/05/rosemarie-trockel/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Rosemarie Trockel">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/annette-lemieux/" rel="tag"&gt;Annette Lemieux&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/arnulf-rainer/" rel="tag"&gt;Arnulf Rainer&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/cindy-sherman/" rel="tag"&gt;Cindy Sherman&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/descartes/" rel="tag"&gt;Descartes&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/elizabeth-sussman/" rel="tag"&gt;Elizabeth Sussman&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/ica/" rel="tag"&gt;ICA&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/rosemarie-trockel/" rel="tag"&gt;Rosemarie Trockel&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/sidra-stich/" rel="tag"&gt;Sidra Stich&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/sigmar-polke/" rel="tag"&gt;Sigmar Polke&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/sophie-calle/" rel="tag"&gt;Sophie Calle&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-phoenix/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/installation/" rel="category tag"&gt;Installation&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/05/rosemarie-trockel/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-3 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-antiquity category-boston-phoenix category-favorites category-museums category-sculpture tag-harvard tag-sackler-museum-harvard tag-sappho tag-william-wordsworth" id="post-3">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/06/a-world-of-clay/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Fragments of Antiquity">
       Fragments of Antiquity
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       June 21st, 1991
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/06/a-world-of-clay/">
       <img alt="Standing Draped Woman from Myrina in the later 3rd century B.C" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1991/06/coroplast-e1271881947356-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       All that we know of Greece has come to us in ruins  armless, headless, faded, fallen, broken, battered, lost in translation. What we have are fragments, fragments that have lost almost everything  except their poetry. But, generation after generation, that poetry has never lost its thrilling, visionary gleam.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/06/a-world-of-clay/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Fragments of Antiquity">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/harvard/" rel="tag"&gt;Harvard&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/sackler-museum-harvard/" rel="tag"&gt;Sackler Museum&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/sappho/" rel="tag"&gt;Sappho&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/william-wordsworth/" rel="tag"&gt;William Wordsworth&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/antiquity/" rel="category tag"&gt;Antiquity&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-phoenix/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/favorites/" rel="category tag"&gt;Favorites&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/museums/" rel="category tag"&gt;Museums&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/sculpture/" rel="category tag"&gt;Sculpture&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/06/a-world-of-clay/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->
    </div>
    <div class="post-9 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-favorites category-museums category-painting tag-edouard-manet tag-berthe-morisot tag-museum-of-art-risde" id="post-9">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/07/dream-lovers/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Dream Lovers">
       Dream Lovers
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       July 12th, 1991
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/07/dream-lovers/">
       <img alt="Berthe Morisot by Edouard Manet, 1872, private collection, Paris" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1991/07/BERTHE-MORISTON-1872-BY-Manet-e1275426223498-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       When Berthe Morisot met douard Manet at the Louvre in 1867, he was 36 years old and married; she was ten years younger and still living with her parents at home. She was lively, intelligent, charming, talented. He was brilliant, difficult, fickle, famous, fascinating. She had long admired him from a distance; he immediately wanted to paint her portrait.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/07/dream-lovers/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Dream Lovers">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/edouard-manet/" rel="tag"&gt;douard Manet&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/berthe-morisot/" rel="tag"&gt;Berthe Morisot&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/museum-of-art-risde/" rel="tag"&gt;Museum of Art RISD&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-phoenix/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/favorites/" rel="category tag"&gt;Favorites&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/museums/" rel="category tag"&gt;Museums&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/painting/" rel="category tag"&gt;Painting&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/07/dream-lovers/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->
    </div>
    <div class="post-5 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-favorites category-museums category-painting tag-elizabeth-vigee-lebrun tag-jacques-louis-david tag-mfa-boston" id="post-5">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/07/elizabeth-vigee-lebrun/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Elizabeth Vigee-Lebrun">
       Elizabeth Vigee-Lebrun
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       July 19th, 1991
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/07/elizabeth-vigee-lebrun/">
       <img alt="Elizabeth Vigee-Lebrun" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1991/07/vigee-lebrun-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Madame Vigee-Lebrun revolutionized the portrait. She despised the powder and stiff clothes that women wore; she let their hair down, and draped them in soft, flowing shawls and painted them looking soft, dreamy, natural, alive. Her paintings helped to create a new look, a new style, a new attitude to life in pre-revolutionary Paris.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/07/elizabeth-vigee-lebrun/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Elizabeth Vigee-Lebrun">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/elizabeth-vigee-lebrun/" rel="tag"&gt;Elizabeth Vigee-Lebrun&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/jacques-louis-david/" rel="tag"&gt;Jacques-Louis David&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/mfa-boston/" rel="tag"&gt;MFA Boston&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-phoenix/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/favorites/" rel="category tag"&gt;Favorites&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/museums/" rel="category tag"&gt;Museums&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/painting/" rel="category tag"&gt;Painting&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/07/elizabeth-vigee-lebrun/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->
    </div>
    <div class="post-21 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-museums category-painting tag-boston-phoenix tag-goya tag-henry-james tag-isabella-stewart-gardner-museum tag-john-singer-sargent tag-mfa-boston tag-trevor-fairbrother tag-velasquez tag-william-butler-yeats" id="post-21">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/08/john-singer-sargents-el-jaleo/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to John Singer Sargents EL JALEO">
       John Singer Sargents
       <span class="caps">
        EL
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        JALEO
       </span>
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       August 28th, 1991
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/08/john-singer-sargents-el-jaleo/">
       <img alt="J.S. Saargent, El Jaleo, 1882, ISGM" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1991/04/El_Jaleo-2-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       In a dark, smoky room, a solitary dancer raises up her arm in a tense, ecstatic movement of inspiration; her other hand clutches the skirt of her dress  a flash of white light gleaming in the dark. You can almost hear the rhythmic weeping of the guitars; you can almost feel beating of the dancers tumultuous heart.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/08/john-singer-sargents-el-jaleo/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to John Singer Sargents EL JALEO">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-808 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-museums tag-alphone-mucha tag-andy-warhol tag-edouard-manet tag-barbara-stern-shapiro tag-baudelaire tag-cezanne tag-edgar-degas tag-henry-james tag-jules-cheret tag-mary-cassatt tag-mfa-boston tag-pablo-picasso tag-pierre-auguste-renoir tag-toulouse-lautrec tag-victorine-murent" id="post-808">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/09/pleasures-of-paris/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Pleasures of Paris">
       Pleasures of Paris
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       September 6th, 1991
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/09/pleasures-of-paris/">
       <img alt="Edgar Degas, Mary Cassatt at the Louvre, 1879, MFA Boston" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/06/Edgar-Degas-Mary-Cassatt-at-the-Louvre-1879-MFA-Boston-e1275793073205-113x150.gif" width="113"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       in a moment, the door will swing back shut, and the cafe will disappear, and then the street singer will vanish, into the street, into the night, never to be seen again. Only here, in this painting, where she is forever caught in the golden net of the Paris night at the moment when she stepped out through the swinging door, onto the street, and into our dreams.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/09/pleasures-of-paris/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Pleasures of Paris">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-998 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-museums category-painting tag-alexei-von-jawlensky tag-beethoven tag-busch-reisinger-museum tag-edvard-munch tag-el-lissitzky tag-harvard tag-lazlo-moholy-nagy tag-lionel-feininger tag-max-beckmann tag-walter-gropius tag-wassily-kandinsky" id="post-998">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/09/busch-reisinger-museum/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Busch-Reisinger Museum">
       Busch-Reisinger Museum
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       September 14th, 1991
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/09/busch-reisinger-museum/">
       <img alt="Max Beckmann, The Actors, 1942, HUAM" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="132" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/06/Max-Beckmann-The-Actors-1942-HUAM-e1276480006144-150x132.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       A crowded stage, and all the players on it. A king, wearing a crown, stabs himself in the heart. A woman looks at her reflection in a mirror, next to a statue of a Greek god. Modern men and women read the newspaper, talk, flirt, and fight with real knives.
       <span class="caps">
        MAX
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        BECKMANN
       </span>
       s The Actors aims to encompass all of Art and Life in thick, sure slashes of paint.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/09/busch-reisinger-museum/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Busch-Reisinger Museum">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/alexei-von-jawlensky/" rel="tag"&gt;Alexei von Jawlensky&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/beethoven/" rel="tag"&gt;Beethoven&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/busch-reisinger-museum/" rel="tag"&gt;Busch-Reisinger Museum.&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/edvard-munch/" rel="tag"&gt;Edvard Munch&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/el-lissitzky/" rel="tag"&gt;El Lissitzky&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/harvard/" rel="tag"&gt;Harvard&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/lazlo-moholy-nagy/" rel="tag"&gt;Lazlo Moholy-Nagy&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/lionel-feininger/" rel="tag"&gt;Lionel Feininger&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/max-beckmann/" rel="tag"&gt;Max Beckmann&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/walter-gropius/" rel="tag"&gt;Walter Gropius&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/wassily-kandinsky/" rel="tag"&gt;Wassily Kandinsky&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-phoenix/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/museums/" rel="category tag"&gt;Museums&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/painting/" rel="category tag"&gt;Painting&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/09/busch-reisinger-museum/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-322 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-museums category-sculpture tag-bauhaus tag-busch-reisinger-museum tag-lazlo-moholy-nagy tag-light-space-modulator tag-sibyl-moholy-nagy tag-walter-gropius tag-william-wainwright" id="post-322">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/10/lazlo-moholy-nagys-light-space-modulator/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Lazlo Moholy-Nagys Light-Space Modulator">
       Lazlo Moholy-Nagys Light-Space Modulator
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       October 4th, 1991
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/10/lazlo-moholy-nagys-light-space-modulator/">
       <img alt="Lazlo Moholy Nagy, LIght Space Modulator, 1922" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1991/10/moholy-nagy-light-space-modulator-1922-c-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="dquo">
        
       </span>
       When the light prop was set in motion for the first time in a small mechanics shop in 1930, I felt like the sorcerers apprentice. The mobile was so startling in its coordinated motions and space articulations of light and shadow sequences that I almost believed in magic.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/10/lazlo-moholy-nagys-light-space-modulator/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Lazlo Moholy-Nagys Light-Space Modulator">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/11/el-corazon-sangrantethe-bleeding-heart/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to El Corazon Sangrante/The Bleeding Heart">
       El Corazon Sangrante/The Bleeding Heart
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       November 1st, 1991
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/11/el-corazon-sangrantethe-bleeding-heart/">
       <img alt="Frida Kahlo with Hummingbird Necklace" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1992/01/Frida_Kahlo_1-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        FRIDA
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        KAHLO
       </span>
       s Self-Portrait with Thorn Necklace and Hummingbird shows her in a jungle with butterflies in her hair and a hummingbird dangling from a thorn necklace that pierces her neck, drawing small red drops of blood. I never painted dreams, she said. I painted my own reality.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/11/el-corazon-sangrantethe-bleeding-heart/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to El Corazon Sangrante/The Bleeding Heart">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-482 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-phoenix category-galleries tag-anne-neely tag-carolyn-boriss-krimsky tag-cheryl-warrick tag-dawn-southworth tag-domingo-barreres tag-elaine-spatz-rabinowitz tag-ellen-banks tag-howard-yezerski-gallery tag-jesseca-ferguson tag-june-southworth tag-karl-lundeberg tag-mark-pevsner tag-paper-prayers tag-paul-shakespear tag-tom-grabosky" id="post-482">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/12/paper-prayersin-the-spirit/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Paper Prayers/In the Spirit">
       Paper Prayers/In the Spirit
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       December 19th, 1991
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/12/paper-prayersin-the-spirit/">
       <img alt="Jesseca Ferguson, Paper Prayer" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1991/12/SCAN0005-e1274295683444-143x150.jpg" width="143"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Many of the artists here are of a generation who rejected the conventional comforts of organized religion  and now they find themselves facing the inevitable mystery of death alone. They are re-inventing rituals that feel authentic to them and finding new ways to satisfy their spiritual needs. Paper Prayers has become one such contemporary healing ritual  a small congregation of artists gathered together In the Spirit.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/12/paper-prayersin-the-spirit/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Paper Prayers/In the Spirit">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/anne-neely/" rel="tag"&gt;Anne Neely&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/carolyn-boriss-krimsky/" rel="tag"&gt;Carolyn Boriss-Krimsky&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/cheryl-warrick/" rel="tag"&gt;Cheryl Warrick&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/dawn-southworth/" rel="tag"&gt;Dawn Southworth&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/domingo-barreres/" rel="tag"&gt;Domingo Barreres&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/elaine-spatz-rabinowitz/" rel="tag"&gt;Elaine Spatz-Rabinowitz&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/ellen-banks/" rel="tag"&gt;Ellen Banks&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/howard-yezerski-gallery/" rel="tag"&gt;Howard Yezerski Gallery&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/jesseca-ferguson/" rel="tag"&gt;Jesseca Ferguson&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/june-southworth/" rel="tag"&gt;June Southworth&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/karl-lundeberg/" rel="tag"&gt;Karl Lundeberg&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/mark-pevsner/" rel="tag"&gt;Mark Pevsner&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/paper-prayers/" rel="tag"&gt;Paper Prayers&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/paul-shakespear/" rel="tag"&gt;Paul Shakespear&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/tom-grabosky/" rel="tag"&gt;Tom Grabosky&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-phoenix/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/galleries/" rel="category tag"&gt;Galleries&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/12/paper-prayersin-the-spirit/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/12/bernd-and-hilla-becher/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Bernd and Hilla Becher">
       Bernd and Hilla Becher
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       December 21st, 1991
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/12/bernd-and-hilla-becher/">
       <img alt="Berndt and Hilla Becher" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/06/Bechers-e1276484182398-150x150.gif" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Bernd and Hilla Becher photographed blast furnaces, water towers, power stations, and other industrial structures, which they called anonymous sculpture. I thought of this show again when I first read W.G. Sebalds books  mysterious, elusive, and strangely moving.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1991/12/bernd-and-hilla-becher/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Bernd and Hilla Becher">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-369 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-books category-interviews tag-camille-paglia tag-coleridge tag-emily-dickinson tag-herbert-golder tag-ovid tag-the-boston-review tag-william-blake" id="post-369">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1992/05/camille-paglia/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Camille Paglia">
       Camille Paglia
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       May 4th, 1992
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1992/05/camille-paglia/">
       <img alt="camille" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/camille-2-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="dquo">
        
       </span>
       Moment by moment, night flickers in the imagination, in eroticism, subverting our strivings for virtue and order, giving an uncanny aura to objects and persons, revealed to us by artists. The sea, Dionysian liquid nature, is the master image in Shakespeares plays. It is the wave-motion within Shakespearean speech which transfixes the audience even when we dont understand a word of it.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1992/05/camille-paglia/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Camille Paglia">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/camille-paglia/" rel="tag"&gt;Camille Paglia&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/coleridge/" rel="tag"&gt;Coleridge&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/emily-dickinson/" rel="tag"&gt;Emily Dickinson&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/herbert-golder/" rel="tag"&gt;Herbert Golder&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/ovid/" rel="tag"&gt;Ovid&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/the-boston-review/" rel="tag"&gt;The Boston Review&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/william-blake/" rel="tag"&gt;William Blake&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/books/" rel="category tag"&gt;Books&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/interviews/" rel="category tag"&gt;Interviews&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1992/05/camille-paglia/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-523 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-books category-interviews category-prints tag-constance-jacobson tag-david-acton tag-deborah-cornell tag-experimental-etching-studio tag-meryl-brater tag-saul-bellow" id="post-523">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1992/11/working-proof-experimental-etching-studio/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Working Proof: Experimental Etching Studio">
       Working Proof: Experimental Etching Studio
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       November 21st, 1992
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1992/11/working-proof-experimental-etching-studio/">
       <img alt="working proof" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/working-proof-e1274462392230-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Ten years ago, I spent a very happy summer working at Experimental Etching Studio, so I was delighted when the Boston Public Library invited me to help shape a conversation among a group of artists from this extraordinary printmaking cooperative.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1992/11/working-proof-experimental-etching-studio/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Working Proof: Experimental Etching Studio">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/constance-jacobson/" rel="tag"&gt;Constance Jacobson&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/david-acton/" rel="tag"&gt;David Acton&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/deborah-cornell/" rel="tag"&gt;Deborah Cornell&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/experimental-etching-studio/" rel="tag"&gt;Experimental Etching Studio&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/meryl-brater/" rel="tag"&gt;Meryl Brater&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/saul-bellow/" rel="tag"&gt;Saul Bellow&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/books/" rel="category tag"&gt;Books&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/interviews/" rel="category tag"&gt;Interviews&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/prints/" rel="category tag"&gt;Prints&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1992/11/working-proof-experimental-etching-studio/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-595 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-antiquity category-archaeological-fragments category-architecture category-boston-globe tag-constantinople tag-daruzziyafe tag-homer tag-iliad tag-istanbul tag-roxelana tag-sinan tag-smyrna tag-theodora tag-versailles" id="post-595">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1993/10/goddesses-empresses-and-femmes-fatales/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Goddesses, Empresses, and Femmes Fatales">
       Goddesses, Empresses, and Femmes Fatales
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       October 31st, 1993
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1993/10/goddesses-empresses-and-femmes-fatales/">
       <img alt="Sappho, photo Nicmi Erol" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1993/10/sappho-e1274664735380-147x150.jpg" width="147"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       For the ancient Greeks, theater was a Dionysian ritual, and in the amphitheater of Pergamon, you can still feel that mythical intensity. The steep incline of the stone seats creates a tremendous focus of energy on the stage. When I stood at the center and sang, I felt my voice amplified, sound waves vibrating in the air.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1993/10/goddesses-empresses-and-femmes-fatales/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Goddesses, Empresses, and Femmes Fatales">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/constantinople/" rel="tag"&gt;Constantinople&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/daruzziyafe/" rel="tag"&gt;Daruzziyafe&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/homer/" rel="tag"&gt;Homer&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/iliad/" rel="tag"&gt;Iliad&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/istanbul/" rel="tag"&gt;Istanbul&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/roxelana/" rel="tag"&gt;Roxelana&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/sinan/" rel="tag"&gt;Sinan&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/smyrna/" rel="tag"&gt;Smyrna&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/theodora/" rel="tag"&gt;Theodora&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/versailles/" rel="tag"&gt;Versailles&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/antiquity/" rel="category tag"&gt;Antiquity&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/archaeological-fragments/" rel="category tag"&gt;Archaeological Fragments&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/architecture/" rel="category tag"&gt;Architecture&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-globe/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Globe&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1993/10/goddesses-empresses-and-femmes-fatales/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-154 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-books category-boston-magazine category-prints tag-dante tag-michael-mazur tag-robert-pinsky" id="post-154">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1995/01/the-inferno-of-dante/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Inferno of Dante">
       The Inferno of Dante
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       January 1st, 1995
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1995/01/the-inferno-of-dante/">
       <img alt="Michael Mazur, Limbo, for Inferno, FSG" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1995/01/Limbo-MM-FSG-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Dantes vision of Hell is filled with terrifying images of transformation, yet its ultimate horror is its changelessness  the unrepentant sinners whose punishment is to embody, forever, their sins. Centuries after its obscure Florentine villains have been forgotten, the poem still rings true as a drama of the inner life, because the heart of the poem is the hope that we can still be changed.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1995/01/the-inferno-of-dante/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Inferno of Dante">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-147 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-magazine category-drawing category-sculpture tag-barry-gaither tag-billie-holiday tag-fernand-leger tag-jasper-johns tag-john-wilson tag-joseph-norman tag-max-beckmann tag-museum-of-the-national-center-of-afro-american-artists tag-paris" id="post-147">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1995/09/dialogue-john-wilson-joseph-norman/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Dialogue: John Wilson/ Joseph Norman">
       Dialogue: John Wilson/ Joseph Norman
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       September 1st, 1995
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1995/09/dialogue-john-wilson-joseph-norman/">
       <img alt="John Wilson,  Martin Luther King, Jr., 2002  Courtesy of the artist and  Center Street Studio" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1995/09/JWilson_MLK-med-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        JOHN
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        WILSON
       </span>
       is a classically trained artist whose lifes work has been a search for enduring, spiritually charged images of African-Americans.
       <span class="caps">
        JOSEPH
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        NORMAN
       </span>
       weaves together all kinds of imagery into elaborate compositions that are elegant, yet full of feeling. For both of these artists, art remains an important way to think about what it means to be human and to have an inner life.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1995/09/dialogue-john-wilson-joseph-norman/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Dialogue: John Wilson/ Joseph Norman">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1995/12/judy-kensley-mckie/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Judy Kensley McKie">
       Judy Kensley McKie
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       December 2nd, 1995
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1995/12/judy-kensley-mckie/">
       <img alt="Judy McKie, Ibis Ascending" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1995/12/Judy-McKie-Ibis-Aascending-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Working in bronze, that most ancient and enduring of materials,
       <span class="caps">
        JUDY
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        MCKIE
       </span>
       s work reveals the power of art to console and heal. Her Bird Fountain has the silent, soaring presence of great mourning monuments. The water makes you feel calm and peaceful, she says. Its nourishing. A life force.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1995/12/judy-kensley-mckie/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Judy Kensley McKie">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/01/emma/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Emma">
       Emma
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       January 1st, 1996
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/01/emma/">
       <img alt="Gwyneth Paltrow as Emma" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1996/01/emma2_gwenyth-paltrow-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Hollywood has fallen in love with
       <span class="caps">
        JANE
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        AUSTEN
       </span>
       . Her scripts feature snappy dialogue; her plots follow the classic formula of girl meets boy; girl loses boy; girl gets boy; her story lines move deliciously from chaos and confusion to harmony and delight. The latest is
       <span class="caps">
        EMMA
       </span>
       , played to perfection by
       <span class="caps">
        GWYNETH
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        PALTROW
       </span>
       in Wedgwood colors, Empire dresses and pearl-drop earrings.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/01/emma/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Emma">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/01/basquiat/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Basquiat">
       Basquiat
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       January 2nd, 1996
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/01/basquiat/">
       <img alt="basquiat" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1996/01/basquiat-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        BASQUIAT
       </span>
       captures the artists yearning and anguish, moments of bliss and the sheer physical pleasure of making art. His later descent into drugs, loneliness, confusion and despair is truly tragic  you feel him pursued by the Furies of greed, racism, and disease, tracking him inexorably down.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/01/basquiat/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Basquiat">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/01/julian-schnabel/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Julian Schnabel">
       Julian Schnabel
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       January 10th, 1996
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/01/julian-schnabel/">
       <img alt="Charlie Parker" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1996/01/charlie-parker-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="dquo">
        
       </span>
       The scene when
       <span class="caps">
        BASQUIAT
       </span>
       is painting  the Charlie Parker and Max Roach riff is from his record collection. Its very heady at that momentSuccess is when youre making the work of art. The moment of perfect sonorous bliss.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/01/julian-schnabel/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Julian Schnabel">

    <div class="post-139 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-magazine category-interviews category-movies tag-eric-bogosian tag-gene-pitney tag-laurie-anderson tag-richard-linklater" id="post-139">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/02/richard-linklater/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Richard Linklater">
       Richard Linklater
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       February 1st, 1996
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/02/richard-linklater/">
       <img alt="Suburbia" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1997/02/suburbia-e1272975671685-124x150.jpg" width="124"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="dquo">
        
       </span>
       Its unfulfilled longing. Its being young. Meet me at 20. I dont know what I want to do. I kind of want to write. You want to be a artist, to express whats going on in your life. Its a way to lose yourself in your discontent. Otherwise youd just go out and shoot and vandalize. Art is more internal.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/02/richard-linklater/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Richard Linklater">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/02/cambridge-a-clef/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Stephen McCauley">
       Stephen McCauley
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       February 2nd, 1996
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/02/cambridge-a-clef/">
       <img alt="The man of the house" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1996/03/SM-the-man-of-the-house-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="dquo">
        
       </span>
       I suppose I read so many biographies because I was trying to understand how people stumbled through their days and their failures and spun their miseries and despair into great art or pathbreaking science or profound enlightenment.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/02/cambridge-a-clef/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Stephen McCauley">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-17 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-maine category-museums category-painting tag-boston-magazine tag-elgin-marbles tag-john-singer-sargent tag-maine tag-mary-cassatt tag-mfa-boston tag-monet tag-theodore-stebbins tag-thomas-eakins tag-thoreau tag-winslow-homer" id="post-17">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/03/winslow-homer/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Winslow Homer">
       Winslow Homer
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       March 2nd, 1996
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/03/winslow-homer/">
       <img alt="Winslow Homer, Northeaster" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1996/03/Winslow_Homer_-_Northeaster.28064408_std-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        WINSLOW
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        HOMER
       </span>
       spent most of his life fishing and painting, reeling in the deep, unfathomable mystery of the sea. His pictures often show somebody gazing out to sea, concentrating on something no one else can see. Maybe its the light on the water, or the wind in the sails, or a boat coming home to shore, or just the flicker of a dream.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/03/winslow-homer/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Winslow Homer">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-979 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-books category-boston-magazine category-interviews tag-herman-melville tag-wyn-kelley" id="post-979">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/04/herman-melville/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Herman Melville">
       Herman Melville
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       April 1st, 1996
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/04/herman-melville/">
       <img alt="Moby Dick, Rockwell Kent" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1996/04/Moby-Dick-Rockwell-Kent-e1276392521867-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="dquo">
        
       </span>
       Give me a condors quill! Give me Vesuvius crater for an inkstand! Friends, hold my arms! For in the mere act of penning my thoughts of this Leviathan, they weary me, and make me faint with their out-reaching comprehensiveness of sweep, as if to include the whole circle of the sciences, and all the generations of whales, and men, and mastodons, past, present, and to come, with all the revolving panoramas of empire on earth, and throughout the whole universe.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/04/herman-melville/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Herman Melville">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/herman-melville/" rel="tag"&gt;Herman Melville&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/wyn-kelley/" rel="tag"&gt;Wyn Kelley&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/books/" rel="category tag"&gt;Books&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-magazine/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Magazine&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/interviews/" rel="category tag"&gt;Interviews&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/04/herman-melville/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->
    </div>
    <div class="post-943 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-magazine category-dance category-interviews category-music tag-calzabigi tag-christopher-hogwood tag-gerard-mortier tag-gluck tag-handel-haydn-society tag-rousseau tag-marie-antoinette tag-mark-morris tag-mikhail-baryshnikov tag-peter-sellars tag-rainer-maria-rilke tag-stephen-mitchell tag-thomas-forrest-kelly tag-yoko-ono" id="post-943">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/04/mark-morrisorfeo/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Mark Morris/Orfeo">
       Mark Morris/Orfeo
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       April 11th, 1996
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/04/mark-morrisorfeo/">
       <img alt="Corot, Orpheus leading Eurydice through the Underworld" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/06/Corot-Orpheus-leading-Eurydice-through-the-Underworld-e1276302554304-144x150.jpg" width="144"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="dquo">
        
       </span>
       It begins with a funereal chorus in the antique style, with cornetto and trombones. And then Orpheus comes in, lamenting his lost love, and sings one single word. Eurydice. He sings it three times. He doesnt say much, but he says everything he needs to say, and the third time he sings it, it sends chills up your spine.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/04/mark-morrisorfeo/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Mark Morris/Orfeo">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-157 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-magazine category-dance category-interviews category-music tag-amadou-hampate-ba tag-beth-soll tag-richard-cornell" id="post-157">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/04/beth-soll-richard-cornell/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Beth Soll / Richard Cornell">
       Beth Soll / Richard Cornell
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       April 29th, 1996
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/04/beth-soll-richard-cornell/">
       <img alt="Beth Soll, photo Richard Grabbert, 1985" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1996/04/beth-phtot-by-richard-grabbert-1985-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Dancer Beth Soll and Composer Richard Cornell are working together on a dance inspired by a book by West African poet Amadou Hampate Ba. Its a long tale, an initiatory allegory, a triumph of knowledge over fortune and power, says Cornell. A quest for God and wisdom, says Soll.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/04/beth-soll-richard-cornell/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Beth Soll / Richard Cornell">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-146 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-antiquity category-boston-magazine category-museums category-sculpture tag-achilles tag-amy-brauer tag-carol-mattusch tag-harvard tag-henry-lie tag-sackler-museum-harvard tag-shakespeare" id="post-146">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/05/the-fire-of-hephaistos/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Fire of Hephaistos">
       The Fire of Hephaistos
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       May 1st, 1996
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/05/the-fire-of-hephaistos/">
       <img alt="bronzes" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1996/06/bronzes-e1273179879812-63x150.jpg" width="63"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       These ancient bronzes, which have long since lost their golden gleam, are still numinous fragments of a vanished world. One statue of young man was recently pulled out of a river; his pale sea-green body is scratched and scarred; but he is still a lovely apparition, reminding me of some lines from Shakespeares The Tempest:
       <br/>
       Nothing of him that doth fade
       <br/>
       But doth suffer a sea change
       <br/>
       Into something rich and strange.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/05/the-fire-of-hephaistos/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Fire of Hephaistos">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-145 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-magazine category-museums category-sculpture tag-anne-nishimura-morse tag-samuel-crowell-morse" id="post-145">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/06/object-as-insight-japanese-buddhist-art-and-ritual/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Object as Insight: Japanese Buddhist Art and Ritual">
       Object as Insight: Japanese Buddhist Art and Ritual
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       June 1st, 1996
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/06/object-as-insight-japanese-buddhist-art-and-ritual/">
       <img alt="Amida Buddha, 11th century, San Francisco Asian Art Museum" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1996/06/Amida-Buddha-SF-Asian-Art-Museum-e1274291893971-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Bodhisattvas with serene, all-embracing smiles; golden flower baskets for carrying lotus petals to purify a sacred space; ritual bronze chimes adorned with peacocks. Each article is incredibly beautiful, but its only when all the articles come together, evoking the presence of the Buddha, that you can understand Buddhist art.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/06/object-as-insight-japanese-buddhist-art-and-ritual/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Object as Insight: Japanese Buddhist Art and Ritual">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/anne-nishimura-morse/" rel="tag"&gt;Anne Nishimura Morse&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/samuel-crowell-morse/" rel="tag"&gt;Samuel Crowell Morse&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-magazine/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Magazine&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/museums/" rel="category tag"&gt;Museums&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/sculpture/" rel="category tag"&gt;Sculpture&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/06/object-as-insight-japanese-buddhist-art-and-ritual/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-987 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-books category-boston-magazine category-interviews tag-florence-ladd tag-james-baldwin tag-radcliffe" id="post-987">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/06/florence-ladd/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Florence Ladd">
       Florence Ladd
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       June 13th, 1996
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/06/florence-ladd/">
       <img alt="Florence Ladd" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1996/06/Florence-Ladd-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="dquo">
        
       </span>
       The sea is a metaphor for transformation, the possibility of crossing over, for becoming someone else, for change, says
       <span class="caps">
        FLORENCE
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        LADD
       </span>
       . Every time Sarah crosses the sea, it changes her. I believe in the unconscious and the way the unconscious enriches our interpretations of life.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/06/florence-ladd/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Florence Ladd">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/florence-ladd/" rel="tag"&gt;Florence Ladd&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/james-baldwin/" rel="tag"&gt;James Baldwin&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/radcliffe/" rel="tag"&gt;Radcliffe&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/books/" rel="category tag"&gt;Books&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-magazine/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Magazine&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/interviews/" rel="category tag"&gt;Interviews&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/06/florence-ladd/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-990 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-magazine category-dance tag-boston-ballet tag-larissa-ponomarenko tag-nabokov tag-pushkin tag-tchaikovsky" id="post-990">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/07/larissa-ponomarenko/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Larissa Ponomarenko">
       Larissa Ponomarenko
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       July 1st, 1996
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/07/larissa-ponomarenko/">
       <img alt="Larissa Ponomarkenko, photo Guido Vitti" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/06/Larissa-e1276428125325-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Ballet is all artifice; but she makes even the Snow Queens dazzling, delicate swirls seem easy and natural. From a distance, she seems fragile, ethereal. But up close, you can see the muscles in her limbs, her graceful neck, her flexible spine. The years of dedication and discipline are sculpted onto her slender frame.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/07/larissa-ponomarenko/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Larissa Ponomarenko">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/boston-ballet/" rel="tag"&gt;Boston Ballet&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/larissa-ponomarenko/" rel="tag"&gt;Larissa Ponomarenko&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/nabokov/" rel="tag"&gt;Nabokov&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/pushkin/" rel="tag"&gt;Pushkin&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/tchaikovsky/" rel="tag"&gt;Tchaikovsky&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-magazine/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Magazine&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/dance/" rel="category tag"&gt;Dance&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/07/larissa-ponomarenko/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-153 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-magazine category-interviews category-music tag-close-encounters-of-the-third-kind tag-francois-truffaut tag-lorraine-hunt tag-media-lab-mit tag-pierre-boulez tag-ray-kinoshita tag-tod-machover tag-yo-yo-ma" id="post-153">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/07/brain-opera/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Brain Opera">
       Brain Opera
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       July 2nd, 1996
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/07/brain-opera/">
       <img alt="Lorraine Hunt Lieberson, photo Richard Avedon, 2003" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1996/07/Lorraine-Hunt-Lieberson-photo-Richard-Avedon-2003-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       The beautiful, beloved voice of
       <span class="caps">
        LORRAINE
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        HUNT
       </span>
       began to rise and spread out through the room, in sweet, sad layers of sound, accompanied by a visual chorus of flashing colored lights, magically transforming the empty, mechanical space into a few moments of unearthly beauty.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/07/brain-opera/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Brain Opera">

    <div class="post-698 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-magazine category-music tag-aretha-franklin tag-diana-ross" id="post-698">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/08/aretha-franklin-diana-ross/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Aretha Franklin/ Diana Ross">
       Aretha Franklin/ Diana Ross
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       August 2nd, 1996
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/08/aretha-franklin-diana-ross/">
       <img alt="Aretha Franklin" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1996/06/Aretha-Franklin-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       When I was young,
       <span class="caps">
        ARETHA
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        FRANKLIN
       </span>
       and
       <span class="caps">
        DIANA
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        ROSS
       </span>
       represented the two poles of womens experience. Dianas sweet, lyrical voice celebrated a womans capacity to abandon herself completely to love. Arethas Respect was the ultimate expression of a womans righteous anger and self-respect. Now I see them both as present-day embodiments of ancient Goddesses, projecting dazzling images of beauty, power, glamour, self-possession, and grace.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/08/aretha-franklin-diana-ross/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Aretha Franklin/ Diana Ross">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-972 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-interviews category-theater tag-commonwealth-shakespeare-company tag-shakespeare tag-steven-maler" id="post-972">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/09/a-midsummer-nights-dream/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to A Midsummer Nights Dream">
       A Midsummer Nights Dream
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       September 12th, 1996
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/09/a-midsummer-nights-dream/">
       <img alt="Commonwealth Shakespeare Company" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1996/09/Commonwealth-Shakespeare-Company-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Shakespeares A Midsummer Nights Dream is about a royal wedding, lovers lost in an enchanted forest, magic spells, and fairy sprites. But mostly it is about imagination. In the course of the play, as the characters move in and out of the world of dreams, certain words repeat over and over again: Fancy. Imagination. Dream. Vision. Transported. Transfigured. Transformed.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/09/a-midsummer-nights-dream/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to A Midsummer Nights Dream">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/commonwealth-shakespeare-company/" rel="tag"&gt;Commonwealth Shakespeare Company&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/shakespeare/" rel="tag"&gt;Shakespeare&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/steven-maler/" rel="tag"&gt;Steven Maler&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/interviews/" rel="category tag"&gt;Interviews&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/theater/" rel="category tag"&gt;Theater&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/09/a-midsummer-nights-dream/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/11/the-eliminator/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Eliminator">
       The Eliminator
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       November 1st, 1996
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/11/the-eliminator/">
       <img alt="The Eliminator" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1996/11/elimiinator.jpg" width="100"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        THE
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        ELIMINATOR
       </span>
       begins as a cop thriller, then turns into a spy movie, then a horror movie with flesh-eating zombies, then a mythical epic, and finally achieves transcendence with an ironic evocation of William Butler Yeats great line of poetry, A terrible beauty is born.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/11/the-eliminator/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Eliminator">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/12/christopher-hogwood/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Christopher Hogwood">
       Christopher Hogwood
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       December 1st, 1996
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/12/christopher-hogwood/">
       <img alt="Portrait of Christoph Willibald Ritter von Gluck" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1996/12/Gluck-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="caps">
        CHRISTOPHER
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        HOGWOOD
       </span>
       has stopped conducting in the traditional stuffed shirt tails and white tie; he now wears a black silk shirt. It gives him the air of an artist  or a monk. The Maestros new clothes are a metaphor for his approach to music: not a dusty, lifeless tradition, but something authentic, full of meaning, and alive.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/12/christopher-hogwood/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Christopher Hogwood">
       Read the full article 
      </a>

     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/12/new-sets-for-nutcracker/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Helen Pond and Herbert Senn">
       Helen Pond and Herbert Senn
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       December 1st, 1996
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/12/new-sets-for-nutcracker/">
       <img alt="Nutcracker Suite" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1996/12/nutcracker_ballet-e1274393912446-142x150.jpg" width="142"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Boston Ballets new Nutcracker sets are the work of a designing couple, Helen Pond and Herbert Senn, who live in a Gothic house in Yarmouthport which they have fully restored with Gothic carving, painted ceilings and lots and lots of quadrifoils, says Herbert. We designed the house and the Nutcracker at the same time. Nutcracker is my life.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1996/12/new-sets-for-nutcracker/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Helen Pond and Herbert Senn">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-141 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-magazine category-music tag-boston-baroque tag-martin-pearlman tag-moart" id="post-141">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1998/05/boston-baroque-abduction-from-the-seraglio/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Boston Baroque: Abduction from the Seraglio">
       Boston Baroque: Abduction from the Seraglio
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       May 21st, 1998
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1998/05/boston-baroque-abduction-from-the-seraglio/">
       <img alt="Martin Pearlman conducts Boston Baroque" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/04/boston-baroque-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Mozarts early opera,
       <span class="caps">
        ABDUCTION
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        FROM
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        THE
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        SERAGLIO
       </span>
       starts out light and comic, gradually grows deeper, more melodic, and more profound, and ends in perfect harmony. He wrote in 1781, at the age of 25, bringing together elements of high art and melodrama into a new form that transcends them both. It was a breakthough for Mozart, says Martin Pearlman, conductor and director of the Boston Baroque.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1998/05/boston-baroque-abduction-from-the-seraglio/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Boston Baroque: Abduction from the Seraglio">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/boston-baroque/" rel="tag"&gt;Boston Baroque&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/martin-pearlman/" rel="tag"&gt;Martin Pearlman&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/moart/" rel="tag"&gt;Mozart&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/boston-magazine/" rel="category tag"&gt;Boston Magazine&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/music/" rel="category tag"&gt;Music&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;span&gt;Comments Off&lt;span class="screen-reader-text"&gt; on Boston Baroque: Abduction from the Seraglio&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->
    </div>

     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1998/08/paula-josa-jones/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Paula Josa-Jones">
       Paula Josa-Jones
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       August 1st, 1998
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1998/08/paula-josa-jones/">
       <img alt="Paula Josa Jones, photo Pam White" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="120" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/1998/08/paula-josa-jones-one-of-the-dreams-photo-pam-white.jpg" width="120"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       <span class="dquo">
        
       </span>
       Its as if they were taking a journey through a landscape and their eyes were caught by something  a memory, or the fragment of a memory, or the memory of a past life  and that pulls them into the movement, says
       <span class="caps">
        PAULA
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        JOSA-JONES
       </span>
       of her new dance,
       <span class="caps">
        GHOSTDANCE
       </span>
       .
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1998/08/paula-josa-jones/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Paula Josa-Jones">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
