    <div class="post-701 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-boston-magazine category-museums category-painting tag-boston-public-library tag-fogg-museum-harvard tag-henry-james tag-isabella-stewart-gardner tag-isabella-stewart-gardner-museum tag-john-singer-sargent tag-mfa-boston tag-richard-ormond" id="post-701">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1999/06/john-singer-sargent/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to John Singer Sargent">
       John Singer Sargent
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       June 29th, 1999
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1999/06/john-singer-sargent/">
       <img alt="Sargent, Carnation, Lily, Lily, Rose, 1895, Tate Gallery" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/J.S.S.-Carnation-Lily-Lily-Rose-1895-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       He was the preeminent portrait painter of his day, and he gave it all up to paint landscapes. His private life is a mystery. His brushwork is still dazzling.
       <span class="caps">
        JOHN
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        SINGER
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        SARGENT
       </span>
       seems to have walked out of the pages of a novel by Henry James, who wrote of him: Yes, I have always thought of Sargent as a great painter. He would be greater still if he had done one or two little things he hasnt  but he will do.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/1999/06/john-singer-sargent/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to John Singer Sargent">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>

    <div class="post-443 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-books category-movies tag-a-s-byatt tag-henry-james tag-joseph-conrad tag-mira-nair tag-moart tag-reese-witherspoon tag-william-makepeace-thackeray" id="post-443">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/2004/05/vanity-fair/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Vanity Fair">
       Vanity Fair
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       May 18th, 2004
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/2004/05/vanity-fair/">
       <img alt="Vanity Fair" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2004/05/Vanity-Fair-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Thackeray endows Rebecca Sharp  that artful little minx  with all the qualities which make his own writing so delightful. He portrays Rebecca as an artist  the lost, brilliant child of a singer and a painter, singing and dancing, scheming and dreaming her way though life.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/2004/05/vanity-fair/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Vanity Fair">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/a-s-byatt/" rel="tag"&gt;A.S. Byatt&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/henry-james/" rel="tag"&gt;Henry James&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/joseph-conrad/" rel="tag"&gt;Joseph Conrad&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/mira-nair/" rel="tag"&gt;Mira Nair&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/moart/" rel="tag"&gt;Mozart&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/reese-witherspoon/" rel="tag"&gt;Reese Witherspoon&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/william-makepeace-thackeray/" rel="tag"&gt;William Makepeace Thackeray&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/books/" rel="category tag"&gt;Books&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/movies/" rel="category tag"&gt;Movies&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/2004/05/vanity-fair/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->

    <div class="post-744 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-books category-theater tag-aeschylus tag-arion tag-bertolt-brecht tag-bob-crowley tag-euripides tag-fridtjof-nansen tag-gilbert-murray tag-samuel-beckett tag-sian-thomas tag-sibyl-thorndike tag-t-s-eliot tag-tony-harrison" id="post-744">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/2008/09/tony-harrisonfram/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Tony Harrison/Fram">
       Tony Harrison/Fram
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       September 30th, 2008
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/2008/09/tony-harrisonfram/">
       <img alt="Dr Fridtjof Nansen [Norwegian Polar Explorer]" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2008/09/Nansen-in-Christiana-1893-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Fram does rise up from the frozen world, uncrushed. The ship, the play, the craft, which is both the ship and poetry, sails on, forward, into the sacred space, where inspiration and despair  the song and the scream  can come together, and embrace.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/2008/09/tony-harrisonfram/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Tony Harrison/Fram">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/aeschylus/" rel="tag"&gt;Aeschylus&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/arion/" rel="tag"&gt;Arion&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/bertolt-brecht/" rel="tag"&gt;Bertolt Brecht&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/bob-crowley/" rel="tag"&gt;Bob Crowley&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/euripides/" rel="tag"&gt;Euripides&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/fridtjof-nansen/" rel="tag"&gt;Fridtjof Nansen&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/gilbert-murray/" rel="tag"&gt;Gilbert Murray&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/samuel-beckett/" rel="tag"&gt;Samuel Beckett&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/sian-thomas/" rel="tag"&gt;Sian Thomas&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/sibyl-thorndike/" rel="tag"&gt;Sibyl Thorndike&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/t-s-eliot/" rel="tag"&gt;T.S.     <div class="post-1062 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-autobiographical-sketches category-furniture tag-carl-rossby tag-den-permanente tag-hans-wegner tag-museum-of-modern-art tag-nasa tag-pasadena" id="post-1062">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/2008/10/hans-wegner-the-bear-chair/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Hans Wegner/ The Bear Chair">
       Hans Wegner/ The Bear Chair
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       October 20th, 2008
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/2008/10/hans-wegner-the-bear-chair/">
       <img alt="Hans Wegner's Bear Chair" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/10/hans-wegner-bear-chair-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Hans Wegner, the legendary Danish furniture-maker, always worked with natural materials like wood and wool, and his furniture reflects both the natural world and abstract art; you can see traces of Brancusi and Picasso in it, as well as animals and trees. He designed more than five hundred chairs during his long and illustrious career. One of them belongs to me.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/2008/10/hans-wegner-the-bear-chair/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Hans Wegner/ The Bear Chair">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
     <!--         &lt;p class="postmetadata"&gt;Tags: &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/carl-rossby/" rel="tag"&gt;Carl Rossby&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/den-permanente/" rel="tag"&gt;Den Permanente&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/hans-wegner/" rel="tag"&gt;Hans Wegner&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/museum-of-modern-art/" rel="tag"&gt;MOMA&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/nasa/" rel="tag"&gt;NASA&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/tag/pasadena/" rel="tag"&gt;Pasadena&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Posted in &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/autobiographical-sketches/" rel="category tag"&gt;Autobiographical sketches&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/category/furniture/" rel="category tag"&gt;Furniture&lt;/a&gt; |   &lt;a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/2008/10/hans-wegner-the-bear-chair/#respond"&gt;No Comments &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; -->
    </div>
    <div class="post-693 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-museums category-prints tag-carl-belz tag-experimental-etching-studio tag-joan-sonnabend tag-joe-zina tag-john-powell tag-lois-foster tag-meryl-brater tag-rose-art-museum tag-susan-stoops" id="post-693">
     <h2>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/2009/04/meryl-at-the-rose/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Meryl at the Rose">
       Meryl at the Rose
      </a>
     </h2>
     <small>
      <strong>
       April 28th, 2009
       <!-- by Rebecca Nemser -->
      </strong>
     </small>
     <div class="entry">
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/2009/04/meryl-at-the-rose/">
       <img alt="Rose Art Museum" class="alignleft tfe wp-post-image" height="150" src="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/Rose-Art-Museum-150x150.jpg" width="150"/>
      </a>
      <p>
       Hundreds of people came to
       <span class="caps">
        MERYL
       </span>
       <span class="caps">
        BRATER
       </span>
       s Memorial Exhibition at the Rose Art Museum. We all believed that Meryl would live on at the Rose, and that many generations to come would have the chance to know her through her art. To close the museum now would be a terrible blow to everyone who loved her  to everyone who trusted their treasure to the Rose.
      </p>
      <a href="http://www.rebeccanemser.com/2009/04/meryl-at-the-rose/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Meryl at the Rose">
       Read the full article 
      </a>
     </div>
